# Network+ Quiz — Full Version History

This file holds the complete release history. The most recent 11 releases stay inline in [CLAUDE.md](./CLAUDE.md) for quick scanning; everything older lives here.

| v4.89.0 | **☁️ Phase C′ cloud-first cert app — Supabase migration + cloud-store + auth-state + builder import (158th ship)**. Replaces the localStorage-only architecture with cloud-canonical user state for signed-in users while preserving the existing 186 localStorage call sites unchanged. Anonymous users still get the full app via localStorage (no behavior change). Signed-in users get cross-device sync via Supabase + an ephemeral localStorage cache, plus a one-time builder import banner that pulls existing local progress into the cloud on first sign-in. **5 new files**: (1) `supabase/migrations/20260506_phase_c_prime.sql` — adds `profiles.role` column + `is_admin()` SECURITY DEFINER helper + RLS policy updates so the admin user can SELECT all rows on profiles + quiz_history + cert_entitlements. Manual one-liner included to promote the owner to admin after first sign-up. Idempotent. (2) `lib/supabase.js` — Supabase client init. Mirrors `landing/lib/supabase.js` (same publishable key, same `.certanvil.com` apex cookie domain so sessions set on certanvil.com are visible at networkplus.certanvil.com). PKCE auth flow. Exposes `window.certanvilSupabase`. (3) `cloud-store.js` — the heart of cloud-first. `USER_DATA_KEYS` Set lists 31 cloud-synced keys (history goes to dedicated `quiz_history` table, everything else into `profiles.metadata` jsonb). Public API: `flush(key)` (debounced 1500ms write), `flushNow()` (immediate, returns Promise), `hydrate()` (cloud → localStorage on sign-in), `clearLocalCache()` (sign-out cleanup), `migrateLocalToCloud()` (bulk one-time import), `getStatus()` / `getLastSyncAt()` / `onStatusChange(cb)`. Wires `pagehide` + `online` + `visibilitychange` events for opportunistic flushing. (4) `auth-state.js` — account pill UI + sign-in flow + auth state machine. Replaces the static `<span class="topbar-avatar">S</span>` with a dynamic `#topbar-account-mount`. Anonymous: renders accent-gradient "Sign in" pill linking to `https://certanvil.com/?action=signin&return=<encoded current URL>`. Signed-in: account pill + dropdown (email + tier + sync status with color-coded dot, Account settings, Visit certanvil.com, Admin Dashboard link only when `role === 'admin'`, Sign out). Listens to Supabase `onAuthStateChange`. On SIGNED_IN: fetches profile, calls `cloudStore.hydrate()`, fires `window.maybeRunBuilderMigration(profile)`. On SIGNED_OUT: `flushNow()` → `signOut()` → `clearLocalCache()` → `renderAnonymous()`. (5) `migration.js` — one-time builder import banner. Detects first sign-in (no `profiles.metadata.migration_v1_at` set + localStorage has `nplus_history`), reads stats (sessions / total Qs / streak best / wrong-bank cards / SR cards / milestones / day-span), renders an inline cyan-gradient banner with "Yes, import" and "Start fresh" actions. On import: calls `cloudStore.migrateLocalToCloud()` then writes `migration_v1_at` ISO timestamp into `profiles.metadata` so the banner never reappears. **Wiring into existing app** (touched 4 existing files surgically): (a) `index.html` — replaced legacy `.topbar-avatar` with `#topbar-account-mount`; appended 6 `<script>` tags in canonical load order (Supabase UMD CDN → lib/supabase.js → cloud-store.js → auth-state.js → migration.js → app.js — order is critical so each module sees its dependencies populated). (b) `styles.css` — appended ~200 LOC of account pill + dropdown styles adapted from `landing/styles.css`. New classes: `.topbar-signin-pill`, `.topbar-account-pill`, `.topbar-account-avatar`, `.topbar-account-email`, `.topbar-sync-dot` (color-coded: synced/syncing/pending/error/offline), `.topbar-account-dropdown`, `.tad-*` family. Mobile breakpoint, reduced-motion gate, light-theme variant. (c) `app.js` — ONE new helper `_cloudFlush(key)` defined near the STORAGE namespace (defensive: try/catch + cloud-store presence check). Then surgical 1-line additions at 24 USER_DATA write entry points: `saveToHistory`, `saveStreak`, `saveWrongBank`, `saveSrQueue`, `setDailyGoal`, `setExamDate`, `setHardcoreMode`, `saveDiagnostic` (+ LAST_DIAGNOSTIC_AT), `unlockMilestone`, `_recordTypeStat`, `saveDailyChallenge`, deep-dive-uses counter, `tbSaveDraft` + `tbPersistAllSaves`, `aclSaveState`, `naSaveMastery` + `naSaveLessonProgress`, `saveSubnetMastery` + `saveLessonProgress` (subnet), `savePortMastery` + `ptSaveLessonProgress` (port), scaffold `saveMastery` + `saveLessonProgress` (covers Acronym Blitz, OSI Sorter, Cable ID via `cfg.storageKey`/`cfg.lessonsKey`), `LAB_COMPLETIONS`, `FIX_CHALLENGES`. Does NOT touch DEV_ONLY/APP_PREFS keys (theme, error log, GH token, API key, AI cache, reports, autobackup, TB UI prefs, port stats, subnet stats — all stay per-device by design). (d) `sw.js` — bumped cache to `netplus-v4.89.0`; added 4 new modules to `SHELL_ASSETS`. Supabase UMD bundle stays on CDN. **Architecture intent**: existing 186 `localStorage.getItem`/`setItem` call sites DO NOT change. Reads stay synchronous. Writes still hit localStorage first; `_cloudFlush` is a fire-and-forget bridge to the debounced cloud queue. localStorage corruption no longer destroys data — cloud has a canonical copy that restores on next sign-in via `hydrate()`. **UAT**: 5072 → **5091** passing (+19 net). New v4.89.0 assertions: 5 script-tag-order regression guards (uses `src="..."` patterns to avoid matching surrounding HTML comments), 1 mount-point existence (#topbar-account-mount), 4 sw.js precache assertions, 2 _cloudFlush helper structural checks, 10 individual write-site flush-hook checks (saveToHistory/saveStreak/saveWrongBank/saveSrQueue/setExamDate/setDailyGoal/unlockMilestone/aclSaveState/scaffold-mastery/scaffold-lessons), 1 new account-pill CSS check. Plus 3 retargeted v4.54.0 tests (legacy `.topbar-avatar` becomes a compat assertion, NEW `.topbar-account-avatar` circular-gradient assertion alongside it). **Playwright: 99/99 still green** — anonymous-user flow is unchanged. **Backwards-compat invariants**: (1) anonymous users see no behavioral change (cloud-store no-ops when isSignedIn() returns false), (2) `_cloudFlush` swallows ALL exceptions so a cloud sync failure never breaks a local write, (3) any USER_DATA write that touches a key NOT in `USER_DATA_KEYS` is silently skipped by cloud-store's filter. Cache: `netplus-v4.89.0`. **158th ship**. **Owner setup required after first sign-up**: run `UPDATE public.profiles SET role = 'admin' WHERE email = 'simi_oremosu@hotmail.com';` in Supabase SQL Editor to promote the owner to admin (Phase C′ migration intentionally doesn't auto-promote — admin role is a deliberate manual step). **Cloud-first SaaS pivot — first cert-app ship after Network+ pass (2026-05-05, 767/900)**. Code freeze lifted with the pass; this is the first day-after-pass infrastructure ship sequencing into the cert-SaaS pivot proper. Recommended path: push to `cloud-first-cert-app` branch + Vercel preview deploy first; sign in via Gmail magic link; confirm sync-status dot turns green + migration banner appears with stats; click "Yes, import"; verify rows in `profiles.metadata` + `quiz_history`; THEN merge to main for prod cutover. |
| v4.88.4 | **🔗 URL `?action=diagnostic` handler — collapses 2 clicks of funnel friction between landing and diagnostic**. Half-1 of Ship B from the cert-mode landing quick-wins mockup (`mockups/landing-cert-mode-quick-wins-concept.html` — user signoff before code per concept-mockup-first workflow, 11 ships in track record now). Pre-fix: visitors had to land on `networkplus.certanvil.com`, see Home page, click the Diagnostic CTA tile, then start the diagnostic — 2 clicks of friction between "I'm interested" and "I'm engaged." This ship adds the cert-app handler that lets the landing button collapse those 2 clicks into 1 by routing direct to `?action=diagnostic` and auto-firing `startDiagnostic()`. **New `_processUrlAction()` function** at the DOMContentLoaded handler hook. Reads `URLSearchParams(window.location.search)`, lowercases + trims `action`, matches against the verb whitelist (currently `'diagnostic'`; future verbs: `streak`, `wrongbank`, `newest`, etc.). On match, **defers 100ms** so the home page paints first then fires `startDiagnostic()` directly. **URL cleanup**: uses `history.replaceState` to strip the query params from the address bar AFTER processing — so a user pressing F5 doesn't re-fire the diagnostic. Hash fragment preserved if present. **Defensive try/catch wrap** at every layer (URL parse, action dispatch, history rewrite) so a malformed URL never crashes the app. **`from=` param** logged via `console.info` for future analytics wiring (e.g., `?from=landing-sample-q` vs `?from=landing-hero` — track which CTA path drove the click). **Hooked into DOMContentLoaded** twice: once as separate listener registered alongside `_v453Init`, once in the readyState-already-loaded fallback path. **UAT**: 5067 → **5072 passing** (+5 net). 5 new v4.88.4 regression-guard assertions: function defined, parses URLSearchParams from location.search, action=diagnostic fires startDiagnostic, history.replaceState cleans URL, DOMContentLoaded hook present. Plus 2 version bumps. **Playwright: unchanged** (would need a contrived test setup to mock URL params + verify diagnostic actually starts; deferred for now). **Behavior**: visiting `networkplus.certanvil.com/` directly = unchanged (no `action` param, handler is no-op). Visiting `networkplus.certanvil.com/?action=diagnostic` = home page paints, then 100ms later the diagnostic auto-fires. **Half-1 of Ship B** — landing-side CTA button + URL construction comes in the next push (separate Vercel project). Cache: `netplus-v4.88.4`. **157th ship**. |

| v4.88.2 | **🐛 Cert-aware domain order across 4 surfaces (Security+ Knowledge Constellation showed wrong titles, plus 3 collateral hardcodings)**. User screenshot of Security+ Analytics → Knowledge Constellation showing the 5 cluster headings as Network+ domain names ("Concepts / Implementation / Operations / Security / Troubleshooting") instead of SY0-701 names ("General Security Concepts / Threats / Architecture / Operations / Governance"). Investigation found **6 places** in app.js with hardcoded Network+ domain key arrays — yesterday's v4.88.1 fix handled the renderSetupDomainGrid path; this commit fixes the remaining 4 that affect Security+ users. **(1) `_computeConstellationData` (line 31016)** — hardcoded `domainOrder` returned -1 for Security+ topic domains, breaking the constellation node positioning. **(2) `_renderAnaConstellation` (line 31077)** — hardcoded `CLUSTERS` literal-keyed map prevented Security+ domain labels from showing AT ALL; the cluster headings reverted to Network+ defaults. Plus the cluster-name render did `c.label.split(' ').slice(1).join(' ')` assuming a "1.0 Concepts" prefix format; now reads full `DOMAIN_LABELS[key]` text. **(3) `computeDomainDistribution` (line 7366)** — **CRITICAL silent bug**: this function maps `n` quiz/exam questions across the 5 domains using `DOMAIN_WEIGHTS[k]`. With Security+ DOMAIN_WEIGHTS having different keys (`threats`/`architecture`/`governance`), the hardcoded `['concepts','implementation','operations','security','troubleshooting']` lookup returned `undefined` → `n * undefined` = `NaN` → broken question distribution → exams could ship with wildly skewed domain proportions. Now reads `Object.keys(DOMAIN_WEIGHTS)` so distribution always matches the active cert blueprint. **(4) Topic Progress accordion grouping (line 1430)** — hardcoded order would bucket Security+ topics into nonexistent Network+ keys. **(5) Exam-domain-breakdown render (line 7966)** — hardcoded display order showed Network+ headings even after a Security+ exam. **Note**: `_buildExamDomainBreakdown` (the data builder feeding the render) was already cert-aware via `Object.keys(DOMAIN_WEIGHTS)` — only the render-side ordering was hardcoded. **Fix pattern across all 4**: `(typeof DOMAIN_WEIGHTS === 'object' && DOMAIN_WEIGHTS) ? Object.keys(DOMAIN_WEIGHTS) : ['concepts',...]` with the Network+ literal kept as defensive fallback. Constellation cluster construction now builds `CLUSTERS` dynamically from `_DOMAIN_POSITIONS` (5 fixed XY anchors) + cert-aware keys + `DOMAIN_LABELS` lookup, replacing the previous hardcoded literal map. **UAT**: 5060 → **5065 passing** (+5 net). 5 new v4.88.2 regression-guard tombstones (constellation domainOrder cert-aware, _renderAnaConstellation builds via DOMAIN_LABELS, cluster name renders full label without split-and-slice, computeDomainDistribution uses Object.keys, exam-domain-breakdown uses Object.keys). Plus 2 retargeted (CLUSTERS-defined regex updated to verify cert-aware construction pattern; constellation `_filterHistoryByTopic` regex window 400→800 chars to accommodate the new domainOrder block) + 2 version bumps. **Playwright: unchanged**. **Behavior**: Network+ deploys unchanged (DOMAIN_WEIGHTS for netplus has the same keys + order as the old hardcoded literal). Security+ deploys now correctly show "General Security Concepts" / "Threats, Vulnerabilities & Mitigations" / "Security Architecture" / "Security Operations" / "Program Management & Oversight" in the Knowledge Constellation, generate questions with correct SY0-701 blueprint weights (12/22/18/28/20%), and bucket Topic Progress + post-exam breakdown into the right 5 SY0-701 domains. Cache: `netplus-v4.88.2`. **155th ship**. Critical question-generation bug had been silently miscalculating Security+ exams since v4.86.0 (cert-pack architecture); fix means Security+ practice exams from this point forward have correct domain proportions. |
| v4.88.1 | **🐛 Security+ Home crash fix — cert-aware bail in renderSetupDomainGrid (user dogfood, exam-prep blocker)**. User screenshot of Security+ deploy: `Something went wrong. Try refreshing the page.` red toast appearing on Home. Diagnostic via Chrome MCP: console showed `[v4.53.0 sidebar init] Cannot read properties of undefined (reading 'replace')` at app.js:36201:12. **Root cause**: `renderSetupDomainGrid()` had hardcoded Network+ domain keys (`concepts`, `implementation`, `operations`, `security`, `troubleshooting`) including in the click handler `onclick="drillDomain('${DOMAIN_LABELS[dk].replace(/'/g, "\\'")}')"`. After v4.86.1 made `DOMAIN_LABELS` cert-aware (loaded from cert pack), Security+ mode populates it with `{concepts, threats, architecture, operations, governance}` — totally different keys. The hardcoded `dk='implementation'` returns `undefined` from `DOMAIN_LABELS`, then `undefined.replace(...)` throws → `window.onerror` catches → red toast. The function is one of three rendered from `_v453Init()` on DOMContentLoaded; the other two (`renderAppSidebar`, `renderTodayPlan`) handle Security+ correctly. **Fix**: cert-aware early-return at the top of `renderSetupDomainGrid` — if `CURRENT_CERT !== 'netplus'`, hide the section cleanly via `is-hidden` class and bail before touching the Network+-only data structures. The Mode Ladder, Today's Plan, Diagnostic CTA, and Pass-Proof banner all stay visible and functional on Security+ Home; only the Network+-specific Domain Grid (with its 5 hardcoded canonical topics per domain) is suppressed for non-netplus certs. Proper cert-aware `domainOrder` + `domainDisplay` + `weightPct` + `CANONICAL_DOMAIN_TOPICS` rebuild remains queued for a future ship; this fix is the "stop crashing right now" patch the user needs for tomorrow's Security+ study session. **UAT**: 5058 → **5060 passing** (+2 net). 2 new v4.88.1 regression-guard assertions ensuring the cert-aware bail stays in renderSetupDomainGrid + the section hides cleanly. Plus 2 version bumps (4.88.0 → 4.88.1) + 1 widened regex window (drillDomain reachability 6000→7000 chars to accommodate the new bail block at the top). **Playwright: 99/99 still green**. **Behavior**: Network+ Home unchanged (early-return doesn't fire for netplus). Security+ Home now renders cleanly without the red error toast. Cache: `netplus-v4.88.1`. **154th ship**. Tonight's third ship after the auth foundation work (44217f4 magic-link auth) and OTP code path (922aa03 held locally). User can study Security+ tomorrow without app crashes. |
| v4.88.0 | **🔧 Five-item rebrand polish — cert copy sweep + landing OG/email/auto-deploy + docs cleanup**. Multi-track ship covering the post-rebrand TODO from earlier in the session. **(1) Cert app hardcoded-copy sweep** — new `_renderCertAwareCopy()` function in app.js runs at DOMContentLoaded after `_renderTopicChipsForActiveCert`. Network+ mode is no-op (static HTML correct); Security+ mode rewrites 9 user-visible Network+/N10-009 hardcodes: diagnostic CTA title, pass-plan-sub, scaled-score labels (results + exam-results), pass-mark threshold (`Pass mark: 720 / 900` becomes `Pass mark: 750 / 900` for Security+), domain-breakdown sub, drills pagehead lede, ed-section-meta tags, legacy hero h1. Plus topic-objective tooltip in `app.js:1293` switched from hardcoded `"N10-009 objective"` to `"${CERT_CODE} objective"` template. Brief Security+ flash on initial load (acceptable since secplus is the private builder URL). **(2) Landing OG image + meta tags** — new `landing/og-image.svg` (1200×630 SVG with M14 logo + tagline + pass-proof pill at scale) + comprehensive Open Graph meta tags + Twitter Card meta tags + canonical URL in landing/index.html `<head>`. Now Slack / Discord / X / LinkedIn / etc. render rich previews when certanvil.com is shared. SVG fallback noted for platforms that prefer raster — PNG export deferred. **(3) Email integration via Resend** — new Vercel Edge function at `landing/api/notify.js`. Receives POSTs from the notify-me modal, validates email + cert, logs to Vercel logs (always — even when Resend isn't configured), then optionally fires two emails via Resend API: confirmation to the signup user + admin notification to `NOTIFY_ADMIN_EMAIL`. | v4.87.2 | **🔧 Security+ branding fixes — Mode Ladder tile names + sidebar S+ / Security+ brand + page title (user dogfood)**. User screenshots after v4.87.1 deploy revealed two real bugs: (1) Mode Ladder tile titles still showed Network+ names ("Networking Concepts", "Network Implementation", etc.) in Security+ mode, with the SY0-701 labels appearing as a *secondary line below* the Network+ headline; (2) Sidebar still showed `N+` mark + "Network+" name even on `secplus-quiz-sable.vercel.app`. **Bug #1 root cause**: my v4.87.1 `_renderTopicChipsForActiveCert` Mode Ladder tile updater used `tile.querySelector('span:last-child')` to find the "label span", but the actual Mode Ladder tile structure has THREE spans — `.mdt-num` (the "1.0"), `.mdt-name` (the bold title — what I should have updated), and `.mdt-meta` (the "23% · 10 Qs" stats line). `span:last-child` resolved to `.mdt-meta`, so my updates wrote the SY0-701 label into the meta line instead of the title — leaving "Networking Concepts" untouched as the headline. **Fix #1**: targeted explicit selectors — `.mdt-num` gets the `idx + '.0'`, `.mdt-name` gets the domain label, `.mdt-meta` gets the cert-correct weight + "10 Qs" string. Tombstone assertion ensures the buggy `span:last-child` fallback doesn't sneak back. **Bug #2 root cause**: `renderAppSidebar()` template literal hardcoded `<div class="sb-brand-mark" aria-hidden="true">N+</div>` and `<span class="sb-brand-name">Network+</span>` — never cert-aware. **Fix #2**: introduced `brandMark` + `brandName` consts at the top of `renderAppSidebar` (`'S+' / 'Security+'` when `CURRENT_CERT === 'secplus'`, else `'N+' / 'Network+'`). Sidebar template uses `${brandMark}` / `${brandName}` interpolation. **Bonus fix #3**: added cert-aware page title swap in the inline `<head>` script — `document.title = 'Security+ AI Quiz'` when `cert === 'secplus'`. Runs synchronously before render so bookmarked tabs show the right title. **UAT**: 5015 → **5025 passing** (+10 net). 10 new v4.87.2 assertions: 3 chip render (`.mdt-name` targeted + .mdt-num/.mdt-name/.mdt-meta all updated + tombstone for span:last-child), 6 sidebar brand (brandMark + brandName declared, both certs covered, sb-brand-mark uses interpolation, sb-brand-name uses interpolation, hardcoded "N+" literal removed, hardcoded "Network+" literal removed), 1 page title (inline script swaps to "Security+ AI Quiz"). | v4.85.20 | **🐛 Exam-split leak fix — per-topic splits were rendering as fake exams in 4 surfaces (user dogfood)**. User screenshot: exam history showed ~50 entries like "900 PASS · 1/1 correct (100%)" + "900 PASS · 2/2 correct (100%)" alongside the actual 780 exam they took. Root cause: v4.81.13's per-topic exam split (which correctly distributes per-topic accuracy data so readiness can attribute exam questions to topics) saves rows with `mode: 'exam', topic: 'BGP', via: 'exam-split', score: 1, total: 1`. **Four surfaces** filter `e.mode === 'exam'` without checking `topic === EXAM_TOPIC`, so each split row was being treated as a separate 1-Q "exam" and scaled to 100-900 (where any 100% gives the max score 900). **Fix**: tightened filter to `e.mode === 'exam' && e.topic === EXAM_TOPIC` in 4 places — **(1) `_renderAnaExams`** (the user-visible exam history list — was showing 50+ rows for one exam), **(2) `getStudyStats` bestExam** (the homepage best-ever exam headline — was showing 900 from a 1/1 split), **(3) `_buildMilestoneCtx` exams count** (was inflating "10 exams completed" milestone — one exam would unlock it), **(4) `_renderAnaExamVsQuiz`** (was skewing the exam-vs-quiz comparison since splits trend toward 100%). **Untouched**: `buildWeightedTopicMap` examBoost (line 11863) + `computeWeakSpotScores` modeBoost (line 12715) — splits SHOULD still get the 1.3× exam boost for accuracy/recency tracking, since they represent real exam-mode questions. **Backwards compat**: pre-v4.81.13 exams have `mode: 'exam', topic: EXAM_TOPIC` and no via marker — these still count correctly through the new filter. **UAT**: 4929 → **4934 passing** (+5 net). 4 structural assertions (each surface filters by topic === EXAM_TOPIC). **1 vm-fixture behavioral test**: fake history with 2 exam summaries + 50 per-topic splits → `_renderAnaExams` renders exactly 2 rows, not 52. **Playwright: 99/99 all green**. Cache: `netplus-v4.85.20`. ~12 LOC across `app.js` (4 filter tightenings + comments), ~70 LOC in `tests/uat.js`. **137th ship**. **Lesson**: when introducing a derivative storage pattern (per-topic splits alongside summary), audit ALL consumers of the source filter (`mode === 'exam'`) to decide whether each one wants summaries-only, splits-only, or both. v4.81.13 added the splits but didn't tighten consumer filters that should remain summary-only. |

| v4.85.15 | **🐛 Mixed-mode readiness invisibility fix — saves per-topic splits + drops e.total>=3 filter (user dogfood, big bug)**. User: *"i feel like these stats are inaccurate, ive studied like 90%+ of everything in the topics on the app"* — they had 611 questions answered with 50/50 topics in Knowledge Constellation, but the v4.85.14 "Why your score?" card showed Coverage 54% / Volume 57%. **Two-bug compound**: **Bug 1** — Mixed-mode quizzes (Deep Scan, Marathon 30/45, Warmup, Daily Challenge, Diagnostic — most homepage tiles) saved a single history entry with `topic: MIXED_TOPIC`. `getReadinessScore` filters out MIXED_TOPIC explicitly to avoid double-counting against per-topic data... but Mixed quizzes never produced per-topic data, so 326+ user questions were completely invisible to coverage/recency/volume. **Bug 2** — even if Bug 1 was fixed, v4.85.8's TOPIC LOTTERY produces ONE question per topic per Mixed quiz, so per-topic splits would all have `total=1`. The `e.total >= 3` filter on the readiness query would throw away every single split. **Two-part fix**: **(1) `finish()`** now branches on `activeQuizTopic === MIXED_TOPIC` and saves BOTH the summary entry (preserved for chronological history + any surface that filters on MIXED_TOPIC explicitly) AND per-topic split rows tagged `via: 'mixed-split'`. Mirrors the v4.81.13 exam-split pattern exactly. Skips `q.topic === MIXED_TOPIC` defensively in case Haiku returns a Mixed-flagged question. **(2) `getReadinessScore`** filter dropped `e.total >= 3`. The intent (filter out 1-2 question noise) is now met by topic-level aggregation in `buildWeightedTopicMap` which sums across sessions per topic — a topic with 1 Q from each of 5 mixed quizzes correctly aggregates to 5 Qs total. **Backward compat caveat**: historical Mixed-mode quizzes saved before this fix can't be reconstructed (per-question topic data isn't preserved in the summary entries). Stats will improve organically over the next few Mixed sessions, not retroactively. **UAT**: 4894 → **4899 passing** (+5 net). 4 new assertions: finish() saves splits when MIXED_TOPIC, both summary AND splits emitted, filter no longer requires e.total>=3, vm fixture confirming filter doesn't reference e.total. **Playwright: 99/99 all green**. Cache: `netplus-v4.85.15`. ~25 LOC added in `app.js` finish() (Mixed branch + summary+splits), ~5 LOC change in getReadinessScore filter, ~75 LOC in `tests/uat.js`. **132nd ship**. **Lesson**: when an aggregation pipeline filters by entry-level constraints (`e.total >= 3`), check whether the producer side ever creates entries that fall under the threshold legitimately. v4.85.8 lottery and the new Mixed-split both produce 1-Q rows that are valid data, not noise. |

| v4.85.13 | **🔄 Constellation tooltip rebuild — fixed top-center + explicit drill button + no auto-navigate (user dogfood, harsh)**. User: *"the functionality sucks i will be honest. it pops up at the bottom... you have to click on it to see it and you only see for a millisecond because once you click on it it immediately takes you to the quiz."* The v4.85.11/12 cursor-following design had three structural problems: (1) on touch devices, `mouseover` and `click` fire simultaneously, so tooltip flashed for ~50ms before the inline `onclick="focusTopic(...)"` navigated away; (2) clamped position landed at the bottom of the map for nodes near the bottom edges (Domain 2/4); (3) cursor-following meant unpredictable position. **Complete rebuild**: tooltip now lives at **fixed top-center** of the map via CSS (`top: 14px; left: 50%; transform: translateX(-50%)`), never moves. Click-to-drill on `<g>` elements REMOVED — drilling now goes through an explicit `<button>` inside the tooltip with onclick bound dynamically to `focusTopic(topicRaw)` at show time. Tooltip stays visible while cursor is anywhere inside the map (including over the tooltip itself, so the button is reachable). Hide trigger changed from per-node `mouseout` to map-level `mouseleave` (which doesn't bubble — listened directly on the map). `pointer-events: auto` on tooltip so the button is clickable. `_anaConstTooltipPosition` helper retired entirely (no more cursor tracking). Show signature simplified from `(evt, nodeEl)` → `(nodeEl)`. Larger styling (16px topic title, larger button, more padding) since it's now a fixed UI element not a floating tooltip. Tier-colored TOP border (was left border) + button background matches tier (green for mastered, accent for proficient, etc.). Mobile breakpoint at <540px stacks tooltip flush left/right with reduced padding. Hint text updated: "Hover any node to see stats · use the button to drill". **UAT**: 4867 → **4878 passing** (+11 net). 11 new assertions (button HTML, show signature, button binds focusTopic, mouseleave wireup, data-tt-topic-raw, top-center CSS, pointer-events:auto, button styling, mobile breakpoint, hint text, position fn retired). 3 v4.85.11/12 assertions updated (border-top vs border-left, click-through-tooltip-button vs onclick-on-g, mouseover+focusin instead of mouseover+mouseout+mousemove). **Playwright: 99/99 all green** — no E2E tests touched the tooltip path. Cache: `netplus-v4.85.13`. ~80 LOC in `app.js` (rewritten show + wireup + tooltip HTML + node attrs), ~70 LOC in `styles.css` (new positioning + button styling + mobile breakpoint), ~60 LOC in `tests/uat.js`. **130th ship** — 3rd attempt at this same feature, finally landed. **Lesson**: when a feature touches hover semantics on touch + desktop, mockup the interaction first. | v4.85.12 | **🐛 Constellation tooltip hotfix — switch from inline handlers to event delegation (user dogfood, same-day fix)**. User: *"the functionality isn't working"* — hovering constellation nodes did nothing despite the v4.85.11 ship. Root cause: inline `onmouseenter`/`onmouseleave`/`onmousemove`/`onfocus`/`onblur` handlers on SVG `<g>` elements injected via `innerHTML` are unreliable across browsers — the attribute serializes but the listener never binds. The `onclick="focusTopic(...)"` worked because `onclick` is the most universally-supported inline event attribute on SVG; the rest are not. **Fix**: removed all 5 inline handler attributes from the `<g>` element. New `_anaConstWireTooltip()` helper uses event delegation on `.ana-const-map` via `addEventListener('mouseover', ...)` etc. — bubbles up reliably from `<circle>` children of `<g>`, works regardless of how the SVG was inserted. Wireup is idempotent (`map.dataset.tooltipWired` guard) so re-renders don't double-bind. Called from `renderAnalytics` immediately after `container.innerHTML = html`. Switched from `mouseenter`/`mouseleave` to `mouseover`/`mouseout` since the latter bubble (delegation pattern requires bubbling), with a `node.contains(e.relatedTarget)` guard to suppress mouseout when moving inside the same node. Keyboard a11y still works via `focusin`/`focusout` (also bubble). **Lesson**: inline SVG handler attributes via innerHTML are a footgun beyond `onclick`. Default to event delegation for any non-click event on innerHTML-inserted SVG. **UAT**: 4864 → **4867 passing** (+3 net). 5 new assertions (helper defined, mouseover/mouseout/focusin/focusout listeners, idempotency guard, called from renderAnalytics, no inline mouseenter on `<g>`). 2 v4.85.11 assertions retired (replaced by delegation versions). **Playwright: 99/99 all green**. Cache: `netplus-v4.85.12`. ~50 LOC in `app.js` (delegation helper + post-render call + inline handler removal), ~30 LOC in `tests/uat.js`. **129th ship**. |

| v4.82.1 | **🎨 Smooth loading bar across all question-fetching flows (user enhancement request)**. User: *"another enhancement, when the questions are loading there needs to be some kind of loading bar aswel."* The `#load-progress` element existed in HTML since v4.43.5 but was wired ONLY into exam mode — regular quizzes, diagnostic, and marathon mode all showed just a skeleton + status text. User asked for the smoothest visual experience, so picked the hybrid pattern that Stripe Checkout, YouTube's buffer bar, and Chrome's pageload bar all use: **determinate stage milestones (no fakery — each event is a real Haiku/Sonnet resolution), eased continuous fill between milestones, plus a shimmer overlay that always animates so the bar feels "alive" even when waiting on a stage.** **The fix — three pieces**: **(1) Unified `_loadingProgress*` module** (3 helpers): `_loadingProgressBegin(initialLabel)` un-hides `#load-progress`, force-resets transition + width to avoid backflow from a previous session's 100%, then nudges to 8% after a 30ms tick (immediate visual "we're working"); `_loadingProgressUpdate(label, pct)` updates fill width + label text; `_loadingProgressFinish()` snaps to 100% + sets "Ready!" label + schedules hide after 400ms. State held in module-scoped `_loadingProgressBar` / `_loadingProgressLabel` references. **(2) CSS upgrade**: `.load-bar` height 4px → 8px (more visible without dominating), `.load-bar-fill` transition `.4s ease` → `1.6s cubic-bezier(0.16, 1, 0.3, 1)` (standard ease-out — races forward then decelerates as it approaches each milestone, creating anticipation for the next jump). New `.load-bar-fill::after` pseudo-element with `linear-gradient` 200% width + `loadBarShimmer` keyframe animation (1.6s linear infinite, sweeps a translucent white band across the fill). Reduced-motion gate kills the shimmer + shortens transition to 0.3s linear. Light-theme variant of the shimmer with stronger white opacity for contrast. **(3) Wired into all 4 fetch flows**: `startQuiz` (8% → 45% post-Haiku → 80% post-Sonnet → 95% post-finalize → 100%), `startDiagnostic` (8% → 60% post-MCQ-filter → 75% top-up → 95% finalize → 100%), `startExam` (per-batch real % — was already this way, just refactored to use the unified module so it gets the same shimmer + transition reset for free), `startBulkQuiz` (marathon — same per-batch real %). **Visual choice rationale**: stage-based-determinate-with-easing was picked over (a) chunky stage jumps (jerky to the eye) and (b) simulated continuous fill that lies about progress (looks polished but gets stuck near 90% if the API is slow). The shimmer overlay is the key — even when the fill width isn't transitioning, the bar still animates, so users never see a "stuck" bar. **UAT**: **15 new v4.82.1 assertions** — 4 module-existence (3 helpers + transition-reset signature check), 5 CSS structural (cubic-bezier transition + shimmer pseudo + @keyframes + 8px height + reduced-motion gate), 4 wiring (all 4 flows call begin + update + finish), 1 tombstone (startExam no longer does the legacy `fill.style.width = '0%'; prog.classList.remove('is-hidden')` un-hide pattern), **2 vm-fixture behavioral tests** — (a) `_loadingProgressBegin` resets transition to 'none' + sets width to 0% + force-reflows + then nudges to 8% (the exact backflow-prevention sequence — direct regression guard against prior-session bar going from 100%→0% over 1.6s before going forward), (b) `_loadingProgressFinish` snaps fill to 100% + sets label to "Ready!" + adds is-hidden to container after the 400ms scheduled hide. Total UAT: 4726 → **4742 passing**. **Playwright: 87/87 still green** — visual smoothness of the bar is hard to assert in synthetic browser context (the bar's mid-fetch state would require mocking Haiku, not worth it for visual polish; underlying functions are vm-tested instead). Validation audit still 64.7% catch / 0% FP. Cache: `netplus-v4.82.1`. ~280 LOC across `app.js` (3 helpers + 4 flow integrations) + `styles.css` (~50 LOC shimmer + transition + reduced-motion + light-theme) + `tests/uat.js` (15 assertions + 2 vm fixtures). **113th ship**. **Monday's 2nd ship** — same-day polish on the v4.82.0 quiz-revisit ship; user dogfooded immediately and surfaced this small but high-value gap. The `_loadingProgress*` module is now the canonical loading-bar API — any future flow that needs progress (validation-audit re-runs, settings export, AI Coach pre-warm) can plug in with 3 lines. |
| v4.82.0 | **🎯 Quiz revisit — editable navigation across all question types (user feature request)**. User: *"one cool thing we need to do which im suprrised we havent done yet is the ability to revisit a previously answered questions whilst ur in a quiz session."* Real gap — exam mode has prev/next + navigator + flag, but regular quizzes had a forward-only flow. Once a question scrolled past, gone. **Three shape-of-solution decisions surfaced up front + locked**: (1) **Editable** (re-pick allowed, not just read-only), (2) **Prev/Next arrows + clickable dots** (matches exam-mode mental model — users learn one nav pattern, not two), (3) **All question types** (regular MCQ + multi-select + order + cli-sim + topology). User approved verbatim → coded directly from mockup. Zero revision rounds. **The fix — three architectural pieces**: **(1) New nav helpers + state inspector**: `_findLogEntryFor(q)` (object-identity lookup in `log[]`), `_recomputeQuizCounters()` (recomputes `score = log.filter(isRight).length` + `answered = log.length`; deliberately leaves `streak` untouched), `_renderQuizNavArrows()` (toggles prev/next-arrow disabled state based on current position + answered-state of surrounding questions), `jumpToQuestion(idx)` / `prevQuestion()` / `nextQuestion()` for click + keyboard wiring. Numbered clickable dots replace the prior 4×18px presentational pills (scoped via `#quiz-prog-dots .qpd-cell` so exam dots stay thin — exam already has its own navigator). 22×22px circles with hover lift + focus-visible + reduced-motion gate. **(2) `render()` revisit branch**: at the end of pristine render, checks for an existing log entry. If found → calls `_restoreAnsweredQuizState(q, entry)` which re-applies correct/wrong/reveal-correct/dimmed markers per question type AND keeps options click-enabled (no more `disabled=true` post-pick), shows the explanation populated from THIS entry (not `log[log.length - 1]` — that bug class would surface stale wrong-explain text after a revisit), surfaces the yellow `#quiz-revisit-banner` ("Revisiting — pick again to change your answer. Score updates; streak stays.") and updates the q-label to *"Question N of M · revisiting"*. Multi-select hydrates `msSelections` from the stored chosen letters; order hydrates `orderSequence`; topology hydrates `topoDevices` from the stored JSON. **(3) `pick()` + `submitMultiSelect()` + `submitOrder()` + `submitTopology()` all get an "if log entry exists, UPDATE; else PUSH" branch**: re-picks update `log[existing.idx]` in-place, then call `_recomputeQuizCounters()` to truth up score+answered, then truth-up wrong-bank (`if (!isRight && wasRight) addToWrongBank` / `else if (isRight && !wasRight) graduateFromBank`). First-pick path unchanged. **Removed**: pre-fix `pick()` had `if (querySelector('.option.correct, .option.wrong')) return;` which silently no-op'd re-picks. Same guard in renderMultiSelect's `btn.onclick`. Both gone. Submit/reset buttons stay visible after submit (not hidden) so re-arrange + re-submit works. PBQ items + zones don't get `pointerEvents: none` anymore. **CLI sim**: re-uses `pick()` for the diagnosis MCQ, so it inherits revisit-aware behavior for free. `_restoreAnsweredQuizState` reveals the hidden diagnosis container. **Keyboard**: `ArrowLeft` / `ArrowRight` wired to `prevQuestion()` / `nextQuestion()` for `onQuiz` (was previously only `onExam`). **Test-only injection hook**: `window._testInjectQuiz(qs)` in app.js — top-level `let questions` doesn't attach to window so Playwright can't seed quiz state without a real Haiku call. The hook resets module state + calls `showPage('quiz') + render()`. Always-safe, no destructive behavior — just zero-API quiz seeding for E2E tests. **HTML**: 2 new nav-arrow buttons (`#quiz-prev-btn` / `#quiz-next-arrow-btn`) inside `.progress-label`, plus `#quiz-revisit-banner` element below the explanation. **CSS**: ~150 LOC — clickable numbered dots + revisit-aware `.now+.done`/`.now+.wrong` combo classes (currently revisiting a previously-correct question shows green-tint with accent ring), nav-arrow circular pills with hover lift, yellow dashed-border revisit banner, `.options.is-revisiting` cursor + filter-brightness hover for re-enabled options, full reduced-motion gate. **UAT**: **23 new v4.82.0 assertions** — 8 helper-existence (3 inspectors + 3 nav handlers + 2 render helpers), 3 HTML structural (2 buttons + banner element), 5 CSS structural (clickable dots + nav-arrows + banner + options.is-revisiting + reduced-motion), 4 wiring (dots are buttons with onclick, pick re-pick branch, pick wrong-bank truth-up, render calls _restoreAnsweredQuizState), 2 PBQ wiring (submitMultiSelect + submitOrder + submitTopology re-submit branches), 2 keyboard wiring (ArrowLeft/Right on onQuiz), 1 streak-invariant assertion (_recomputeQuizCounters must NOT touch streak), 1 guard-removed tombstone, **5 vm-fixture behavioral tests** — (a) `_recomputeQuizCounters` recomputes score/answered from log + leaves streak untouched, (b) `_findLogEntryFor` matches by question object identity (not by stem string), (c) **pick re-pick wrong→right** updates entry + bumps score 0→1 + calls graduateFromBank exactly once + does NOT call addToWrongBank + leaves streak untouched, (d) **pick re-pick right→wrong** updates entry + drops score 1→0 + calls addToWrongBank exactly once + does NOT call graduateFromBank + leaves streak untouched (most important fixture — direct regression guard against streak-inflation on score downgrades), (e) Playwright spec presence check (the meta-guard pattern from v4.81.31). | v4.81.30 | **🎯 SR review interactive answering — commit-before-reveal across all 3 modes (user pedagogy feedback)**. User: *"i want to be able to actually answer these questions by clicking on the answer i think it is. because right now im just reading the answers and self grading. the risk of this is that someone can just lie and say yeah i knew that when deep down they didnt."* Sharp pedagogical critique. The v4.81.27/28 self-grade path showed the explanation IMMEDIATELY before any user commitment, structurally encouraging self-deception. Anki, Quizlet, every serious flashcard app forces commitment-before-reveal for exactly this reason. **The fix — 3 review modes, all gated behind user commitment**: **Mode 1: MCQ AUTO-GRADE** (mostly unchanged from v4.81.27) — pick one option → reveal → auto-check (✓ green for correct, ✗ red for wrong pick) → confidence row (Confident/Uncertain on win, "Got it wrong" on miss). **Mode 2: MULTI-SELECT AUTO-GRADE (NEW)** — toggle multiple options freely → click "Reveal answer →" Submit button (enabled at ≥2 picks, shows "Pick 2 answers · 1 selected" hint with live count) → reveal with three-marker system: ✓ green for correct picks (`is-correct`), ✗ red for wrong picks (`is-wrong`), ⚠ amber-dashed for missed correct picks (`is-missed`, NEW CSS class with the "missed" inline label). All-or-nothing for SR scheduling — fully correct gets Confident/Uncertain, anything else (wrong pick OR missed correct) routes to "Got it wrong" + shows what the correct set was. **Mode 3: COMMIT-THEN-SELF-GRADE** (refactor of legacy fallback) — kicks in only when the card has truly broken data (legacy null-answer MCQs from the v4.81.27-fixed addToSrQueue corruption, OR multi-select cards somehow missing the answers array). User picks ONE option → reveal explanation (no correctness markers because we don't have the answer key) → 3 self-grade buttons (Confident/Uncertain/Wrong). User still commits BEFORE seeing the explanation, so the self-deception loophole is closed even in this fallback. **State changes**: `_srSession.pickedLetters` (Set, NEW) tracks multi-select picks; `pickedLetter` (string) tracks single-pick for MCQ + commit-self-grade modes; both reset in `srMarkConfidence` on advance. **New handlers**: `srToggleMultiPick(letter)` (toggle on/off in pickedLetters Set), `srSubmitMultiPick()` (sets revealed=true + re-renders, guards on min 2 picks). **Removed**: v4.81.28's `_srSession.revealed = true` hack in the self-grade render — no longer needed because all paths now properly flip revealed=true on user commitment, not on render. Tombstone UAT asserts the hack stays gone. **CSS**: new `.sr-option.is-missed` (amber dashed border + "⚠ missed" inline label), `.sr-multi-submit-row` (centered submit + hint), `.sr-multi-submit-btn` (accent gradient when enabled, dim when disabled). All three new styles get reduced-motion-aware transitions. **UAT**: **14 new v4.81.30 assertions** + **3 retired/retargeted older fixtures** (v4.81.27/28 fallback assumptions no longer apply) — 11 structural (toggle handler defined, submit handler defined, pickedLetters Set initialized, pickedLetters cleared on advance, tombstone for v4.81.28 hack, 3-mode structure verified, multi-auto Submit row, is-missed marker, ≥2 pick guard, .sr-option.is-missed CSS, .sr-multi-submit-btn CSS), **3 vm-fixture behavioral tests** — (a) **multi-select pick → submit → reveal flow** end-to-end: render starts with disabled Submit, two picks enable Submit, Submit reveals with correct picks marked is-correct; (b) **wrong pick + missed correct render correct markers**: user picks A (correct) + B (wrong), misses C (correct) → asserts A=is-correct, B=is-wrong, C=is-missed, "Got it wrong" outcome only; (c) **commit-then-self-grade requires pick before reveal**: pre-pick render has no explanation + no self-grade buttons + clickable options; post-pick render has all 3. All three fixtures are direct regression guards against the self-deception loophole. Total UAT: 4672 → **4686** passing. Validation audit still 64.7% catch / 0% FP. Playwright: **79/79** still green. Cache: `netplus-v4.81.30`. **~280 LOC** across `app.js` (renderer rewrite + 2 new handlers + state changes) + `styles.css` (3 new style blocks) + `tests/uat.js` (14 assertions + 3 retargets). **110th ship**. **Sunday's 25th ship** (cluster started Sunday continues into early Monday). The pedagogy fix is fundamental — SR review now tests recall, not honesty. Pattern crystallized: **flashcard apps that don't force commit-before-reveal are training the wrong skill** (memory of having read vs memory of having recalled). |
| v4.81.29 | **🎯 Multi-select prompt quality criteria (user dogfood — pedagogy issue, not render bug)**. User observation: *"i will get one select right but then the other final selection is almost always wrong because the answer is not so obvious."* Real-world cert-prep frustration — and not a code bug, a Haiku question-quality pattern. **Diagnosis**: pre-fix the multi-select prompt section in `_fetchQuestionsBatch` only specified the JSON SCHEMA, not the QUALITY CRITERIA. Haiku optimised "make this hard" → produced the worst possible multi-select shape: 1 obvious-correct + 1 obscure-correct + 2 distractors borrowed from adjacent topics that "feel right." User picks obvious-correct + plausible-distractor → partial credit + frustration. That's the OPPOSITE of how CompTIA writes multi-select — real exam multi-selects test BREADTH (do you know multiple core facts apply?), not obscurity (do you know the buried trivia point?). **Fix**: inserted a `CRITICAL — MULTI-SELECT QUALITY CRITERIA` block right after the multi-select schema spec in the PBQ instructions. Five guidance points: (1) BOTH correct answers must be core, well-known facts at similar levels of prominence — no obvious-vs-obscure imbalance; (2) DISTRACTORS must be factually wrong about the topic (not "less correct" or borrowed from adjacent topics); (3) explicit warning against the "1 obvious + 1 obscure + 2 plausible-adjacent" trap that produces frustration without testing real understanding; (4) explanation must enumerate WHY each correct answer is correct (1-2 sentences each) AND WHY each distractor is wrong (with specific factual error, not vague "less applicable"); (5) stems should ask what IS true / IS valid / DOES apply — not "best fit" / ranking / superiority comparisons. **Affects**: every future multi-select Haiku generates — across diagnostic, regular quizzes, exam simulator, marathon mode. **No effect** on existing wrong-bank or SR queue entries (those keep their original prompt-shaped questions). Existing 200-exemplar `QUESTION_EXEMPLARS` few-shot bank already follows this style — so the new criteria just makes the pattern explicit instead of relying on Haiku to infer it from examples. **UAT**: **7 new v4.81.29 assertions** — structural checks that the new prompt criteria block exists and contains all 5 quality directives (CORE / well-known framing, no-obscure rule, factually-wrong distractor rule, adjacent-topic-trap warning, enumerate-each-correct-and-each-distractor explanation rule), plus a placement assertion that the criteria live inside `_fetchQuestionsBatch` (not orphaned). No vm-fixture for prompt content — quality verification will come from real-world exam-prep observation across the next few quizzes. Total UAT: 4665 → **4672** passing. Validation audit still 64.7% catch / 0% FP. Playwright: **79/79** still green. Cache: `netplus-v4.81.29`. ~30 LOC of prompt copy + UAT. **109th ship**. **Sunday's 24th ship** — closes a real exam-prep frustration the user has been working around. Not a render bug. Not a schema bug. A QUALITY bug at the AI generation layer. Worth tracking how often partial-credit-on-multi-select shows up in the next week. If still frequent → escalate to Layer B (Sonnet validator pass that explicitly grades multi-select balance). |
| v4.81.28 | **🐛 SR review — 3 follow-up bugs after v4.81.27 dogfood (user said "still buggy")**. v4.81.27 fixed the render path so multi-select cards finally showed content (read-only options + self-grade banner + 3 confidence buttons), but a comprehensive audit tonight found 3 more bugs — one critical that broke the self-grade path entirely, and two latent issues from the original SR queue design. **Bug 1 (CRITICAL — blocks the user)**: `srMarkConfidence` had a defensive `!_srSession.revealed` early-return guard. For self-grade cards, `revealed` stays `false` (the user never picks an option that triggers `srPickAnswer` to set it true), so clicking any of the 3 confidence buttons returned early and **did absolutely nothing**. User stuck on every multi-select card after v4.81.27 deploy. **Fix 1**: set `_srSession.revealed = true` in the self-grade render branch. Self-grade is "already revealed" because the explanation renders immediately, so flipping the flag here is semantically correct AND it preserves the existing defensive guard for the auto-grade path (revealed stays false until the user picks an option in MCQ mode). **Bug 2 (latent since SR queue shipped, surfaced by v4.81.27 fix)**: `addToSrQueue` re-enrollment fired `_srSchedule(entry, 'wrong')` but never refreshed the question payload. Any legacy entry with the v4.81.27-fixed `answer: null` corruption would stay corrupt forever — even after re-encounter — so the v4.81.27 self-heal couldn't actually heal anything. **Fix 2**: on re-enrollment, overwrite `entry.options / answer / answers / items / correctOrder / type / topic / difficulty / explanation` with the fresh values from the current `q`. Legacy corrupt entries now self-heal on the next time the user gets that question wrong. **Bug 3 (silent corruption since SR queue shipped)**: `addToSrQueue` accepted any `q.type`. Order / cli-sim / topology PBQs were enrolled into the queue but rendered with empty bodies (no `card.options`, no items rendering, just stem + self-grade fallback with no useful content). **Fix 3**: filter at enrollment — `allowedTypes = new Set(['mcq', 'multi-select'])`. Order / cli-sim / topology types return `null` without enrolling. Wrong-bank still tracks the miss; SR queue stays focused on review-able question types. **UAT**: **6 new v4.81.28 assertions** — 3 structural (revealed=true in self-grade branch, payload refresh on re-enroll, allowedTypes filter), **3 vm-fixture behavioral tests** — (a) end-to-end self-grade flow: render multi-select card → assert `revealed=true` is set → call `srMarkConfidence('correct-confident')` → assert index advanced + tally updated (the exact post-v4.81.27 bug case); (b) re-enrollment heals legacy null-answer entry: pre-seed queue with `answer: null` corrupt entry → re-enroll with valid `answer: 'C'` → assert payload now correct; (c) order/cli-sim/topology types rejected at enrollment: 3 PBQ types return null + 0 enroll, mcq + multi-select both enroll + 2 in queue. | v4.81.27 | **🐛 SR review render — three latent bugs uncovered by user dogfood (multi-select stem with no options visible)**. User screenshot of SR Review page: a multi-select question stem rendered correctly ("(Choose TWO) A network architect is evaluating WAN technologies...") but **no answer options below it**. Empty card body. Investigation revealed three layered bugs that compounded: **(1) Schema mismatch in `_renderSrCard`** — the renderer expected `card.options` as an array (`Array.isArray(opts)` check) and built buttons via `opts.map((o, idx) => ...)`, but the live app stores options as a letter-keyed object `{A: '...', B: '...', ...}` matching `renderMCQ`. The `Array.isArray()` check failed, options never rendered. Same bug class as v4.81.5 diagnostic-options schema mismatch. **(2) Answer-preservation bug in `addToSrQueue`** (latent since SR queue shipped) — `answer: typeof q.answer === 'number' ? q.answer : null` had the wrong type guard. The app stores MCQ answers as letter strings (`'A'`, `'B'`), so `typeof 'A' !== 'number'` always evaluated false → every MCQ ever enrolled was saved with `answer: null`. Auto-grading was impossible even if options had rendered. **(3) Multi-select unsupported entirely** — even with the above fixed, a multi-select card has 5 options + an `answers: ['A','C']` array; the SR review card was built as a simple radio-style flashcard. **Three-fix ship**: **Fix A**: rewrote `_renderSrCard` to normalise options into `optionLetters[]` + `optionMap{}` regardless of stored shape (object or array), then build buttons by iterating sorted letters. Coerces numeric-index legacy answers to letter form for the auto-grade compare. **Fix B**: changed `addToSrQueue` to preserve `q.answer` as-is (`(q.answer != null) ? q.answer : null`) — strings, numbers, both work. **Fix C**: added a self-grade fallback path. When the card can't be auto-graded (`type === 'multi-select'` OR `answer === null` from the legacy enrollment bug), show options READ-ONLY (so the user can reason), display the explanation immediately, and present three confidence buttons (Confident / Uncertain / Wrong) without an auto-check. | v4.81.25 | **🐛 Order-question quality fix — Implement-before-Verify invariant + conflated-step rejection (user dogfood, exam-related)**. User screenshot of a Hard ordering question on the CompTIA troubleshooting methodology: the "correct order" the app showed had item 4 = *"Document findings AND implement a permanent solution or workaround"* — and the order placed verify (item 3) BEFORE this conflated implement+document item. **Two structural bugs in one question**: (1) item 4 conflated CompTIA Step 5 (Implement) with Step 7 (Document), which are non-adjacent in the methodology — Step 6 (Verify) sits between them; (2) even given the malformed item, the order put verify before implement, which is logically impossible (you can't verify a solution you haven't implemented yet). **Why the existing validator missed it**: `_tbTroubleshootingOrderOk` (v4.62.2) had a tight stem-detection gate requiring "comptia" + "methodology" / "X-step" — but the user's stem just said *"Arrange the following troubleshooting steps in the correct order when diagnosing a network connectivity issue."* No "comptia". No "methodology". So the existing methodology rules didn't fire. **Three-layer fix**: **Layer 0 (gate widening)**: validator now also fires on (a) generic "troubleshooting steps" + ordering keywords ("order"/"sequence"/"arrange") in the stem, (b) "diagnostic" + ordering, (c) item-keyword combo (Identify-the-problem + Document-findings both present) regardless of stem wording — that last one is the most robust because if the items themselves describe the methodology, we should enforce its rules even if Haiku's stem wording is loose. **Layer A (Implement-before-Verify ordering invariant)**: regex matches `\bimplement(?:ing)?\b ... \b(?:solution|fix|workaround|change|plan)\b` for the implement item, `\b(?:verify|verification)\b ... (?:solution|connectivity|functionality|resolved|restored|preventive|fixed)\b` for verify. If both present in different items and `posImpl >= posVer`, reject. **Layer B (conflated-step rejection)**: regex `\bimplement(?:ing)?\b ... \b(?:solution|fix|workaround|plan)\b` AND `\bdocument(?:ing)?\b ... \b(?:findings?|actions?|outcomes?)\b` in the same item — auto-reject. Steps 5 and 7 are non-adjacent; combining them in one item is structurally malformed regardless of which order the grader picks. **The bug class**: same family as v4.81.16 (multi-select stem-vs-answer-count + canonical fact lock) — generic structural validator + specific content invariant. Order-question equivalent. **UAT**: **9 new v4.81.25 assertions** — 5 structural (gate-widened keywords, Identify+Document combo gate, implementIdx + verifyIdx variables declared, Implement-before-Verify ordering enforcement, conflated-keyword detection), **4 vm-fixture behavioral tests** — (a) the EXACT user-reported bug case rejected (4 items including "Document findings AND implement..." with the same correctOrder the app produced); (b) Implement-after-Verify rejected even with clean (non-conflated) items; (c) correct 6-step methodology ordering accepted (regression guard, no false positive); (d) non-troubleshooting order question (OSI layer ordering) passes through unchanged. Total UAT: 4637 → **4646** passing. Validation audit: still 64.7% catch / 0% FP — new layers add rejection paths without false-positive any of the 23 broken-corpus or curated-good fixtures. Playwright: **79/79** still green. Cache: `netplus-v4.81.25`. ~80 LOC across `app.js` + `tests/uat.js`. **105th ship**. **Sunday's 20th ship** — second exam-related dogfood fix in the same evening (paired with v4.81.24 fix-forward). Pattern repeats: the user's exam prep is the highest-fidelity quality engine we have. |

One-line change in `tests/deploy-verify.js`. **Prevention**: added a UAT cross-check that parses `REQUIRED_IDS` out of `tests/deploy-verify.js` and asserts every ID in the list is present in `index.html`. Catches future drift locally before any push: if a future ship removes a DOM element listed in `REQUIRED_IDS` without updating the list, UAT fails immediately with a specific error message naming the missing IDs. **Audit-pattern lesson**: cleanup-pass ships that remove DOM elements need to also walk `tests/deploy-verify.js`'s `REQUIRED_IDS` (and any other hard-coded element-presence lists). Filed mentally as "external-test sync check" — same pattern as updating `tests/validation-audit.js` when a new validator helper joins the pipeline (v4.81.16 lesson). **Issue #267 closed** as part of this ship — auto-opened by Deploy Verification workflow on v4.81.23 failure. **UAT**: **1 new v4.81.24 assertion** — parses `REQUIRED_IDS` constant from deploy-verify.js, cross-checks every id against index.html, fails loud with the missing list if any drift. Total UAT: 4636 → **4637** passing. Playwright: **79/79** still green. Cache: `netplus-v4.81.24`. ~10 LOC. **104th ship**. **Sunday's 19th ship** — same-day fix-forward for v4.81.23's deploy-verification false alarm. The cleanup arc is fully closed now: v4.81.18 → v4.81.23 (consolidation + cleanup) + v4.81.24 (sync the verifier). |

| v4.81.22 | **🧹 Hide `#today-section` wrapper when all children effectively hidden (user dogfood after v4.81.21)**. User screenshot post-v4.81.21 deploy showed an empty pill-shaped card containing just the "TODAY" title — no daily goal ring, no streak defender, no daily challenge, no consolidated plan card, nothing. The wrapper was rendering as visible because `renderTodaySection()` always called `section.classList.remove('is-hidden')` regardless of children state. **Diagnosis** — historical assumption broke: the original v4.41.0 comment said *"Daily goal card is always visible, so the section is always shown"* — true at the time, but: (a) the v4.54.0 hero v2 redesign added `body.hero-v2-active #page-setup .today-section .daily-goal-card { display: none !important; }` which hides the goal card via CSS (the `is-hidden` class isn't applied, but the element doesn't render), (b) v4.81.18 consolidation made `#todays-focus`, `#rotation-row`, `#session-banner` permanent hidden compat shims, (c) v4.81.18's new `#today-plan` correctly hides itself when `isStudyPlanDoneToday()` returns true. With the user's state (plan done today, streak healthy, daily challenge done) — every candidate child was either hidden via class or hidden via the hero-v2 CSS rule. The wrapper had nothing to wrap, but stayed visible. Result: orphan "TODAY" pill with no content, exactly the same visual-noise pattern v4.81.18 set out to eliminate. **Fix**: rewrote `renderTodaySection()` to actually compute child visibility correctly: walks 4 candidate IDs (`#daily-goal-card`, `#streak-defender`, `#daily-challenge-card`, `#today-plan` — drops the v4.81.18 compat shims since they're permanently hidden anyway), checks `el.classList.contains('is-hidden')` for each, AND checks `body.hero-v2-active` to treat `#daily-goal-card` as effectively hidden when the hero v2 CSS rule applies. If no candidate is effectively visible, adds `is-hidden` to the wrapper itself. Else removes it (existing behavior). Early-bails-loop with `break` on first visible child for minimal cost. **Done shape** — when SR card + Pass Plan tile + Mode Ladder are doing all the prescriptive work and today-section has nothing meaningful to add, the page now flows cleanly from Pass Plan → SR review → Mode Ladder without the orphan TODAY pill. When ANY child has content (e.g. unfinished daily challenge, active streak warning, or active plan), the wrapper shows as before — no behavior change in that case. **Audit-pattern lesson reinforced**: container visibility must be computed from children's *effective* visibility, not just the `is-hidden` class. CSS hide rules (`display: none !important`) need to be considered too. Same lesson as v4.81.20 (audit miss extended beyond the named container) — this time extended to "audit miss in a single function's assumptions." **UAT**: **6 new v4.81.22 assertions** — 4 structure (#today-plan in candidate list, hero-v2-active accounted for, conditional add/remove of is-hidden, tombstone for the retired comment), **2 vm-fixture behavioral tests** — (a) section hidden when daily-goal is hero-v2-hidden + today-plan is is-hidden + others is-hidden (mirrors the user's exact dogfood state); (b) section visible when ANY candidate has content (daily-challenge-card visible despite hero-v2 hiding daily-goal-card). | v4.81.19 | **🔧 Comma-safe `Multi:` topic parser (pre-existing bug spotted during v4.81.17 Domain Drill ship)**. 3 topic names contain literal commas: `'NTP, ICMP & Traffic Types'`, `'SDN, NFV & Automation'`, `'Firewalls, DMZ & Security Zones'`. All 4 sites that parse the `'Multi: <topic, topic, ...>'` sentinel used naive `.split(',')`, mis-segmenting those topics into separate items (e.g. "NTP" + "ICMP & Traffic Types" instead of the canonical name). Bug got more visible with v4.81.17 Domain Drill (3 of 5 domain presets contain a comma-named topic) — Haiku was being told to write questions matching mis-split topic strings, history filtering missed them, multi-count over-reported. Mostly cosmetic in practice (Haiku still produces reasonable questions; per-topic history saves via `q.topic` not the multi-list) but worth fixing for correctness. **Fix**: new `_parseMultiTopicSentinel(qTopic)` helper near `TOPIC_DOMAINS` definition does greedy longest-match against `Object.keys(TOPIC_DOMAINS)` sorted by length descending, so multi-word topic names with commas are preserved verbatim. Accepts both full sentinel (`'Multi: A, B'`) and bare body (`'A, B'`). Falls back to the legacy naive split when `TOPIC_DOMAINS` isn't defined (defensive — should never happen in practice). All 4 split sites updated: (a) `_pickExemplarsForTopic` first-topic extraction for prompt-injection exemplar pick, (b) `_filterHistoryByTopic` multi-list `.includes(topic)` check (drives Progress page topic-rollup + Study Plan ranking), (c) `startQuiz`'s `_multiCount` (display count for the loading message), (d) `_fetchQuestionsBatch` Multi: distribution prompt (highest-impact — feeds Haiku the canonical topic list it must match `.topic` field against). Each call site keeps a `(typeof _parseMultiTopicSentinel === 'function' ? ... : <legacy>)` ternary so the legacy parser stays as a defensive fallback if the helper is somehow unavailable. **Discovery during ship**: user dogfood screenshot revealed that the v4.81.18 Today consolidation missed retiring the v4.54.0 `#focus-banner` (a separate prescriptive surface OUTSIDE the today-section) — it's still rendering "Seven questions per topic, mixed difficulty. Your fastest route to exam-ready" via `renderSetupFocusBanner()`. The new `#today-plan` is correctly hidden when `isStudyPlanDoneToday()` returns true (post-session today), but the focus-banner doesn't share that gate. Filed as v4.81.20 follow-up — same audit pattern as v4.81.18 but extended to the orphan banner. **UAT**: **11 new v4.81.19 assertions** — 4 helper structure (function defined + sort-by-length-desc + accepts-both-shapes + fallback-defense), 4 wiring (4 call sites use the helper), **3 vm-fixture behavioral tests** — (a) all 3 comma-containing topics in one Multi: sentinel parsed verbatim alongside non-comma topics (5 topics in, 5 out, all preserved); (b) regression vs naive split — naive over-segments to 3 pieces and chops "NTP" off the front, new parser keeps "NTP, ICMP & Traffic Types" intact (2 pieces total); (c) parser accepts full sentinel + bare body equivalently + handles empty/null defensively. Plus 2 existing structural-regex windows widened (v4.57.4 200→500/100→300; v4.58.0 100→250) to accommodate the new ternary fallback wrapper. Total UAT: 4601 → **4612** passing. Playwright: **79/79** still green. Cache: `netplus-v4.81.19`. ~80 LOC across `app.js` (helper + 4 call site updates) + `tests/uat.js` (11 new + 2 widened). **99th ship**. **Sunday's 14th ship**. Closes the comma-split correctness gap; sets up v4.81.20 (focus-banner retirement). |

| v4.81.16 | **🐛 Question-quality bugfix — "Which TWO" Wi-Fi channels slip-through (user dogfood after v4.81.15 ship)**. User screenshot during a Foundational quiz: a multi-select Q5 asked *"Which TWO of the following are non-overlapping frequency channels in the 2.4 GHz Wi-Fi band..."* — pedagogically wrong because the canonical N10-009 fact is the 1/6/11 **trio**, not a pair. Submit was disabled with "Select 2 answers" forcing the user to pick fewer than the right answer. **Two failure modes converged**: (a) Haiku produced a "Which TWO" stem when the only fact-aligned correct answer is "Which THREE = 1, 6, 11", (b) `_groundTruthOk` early-returned on `getQType(q) !== 'mcq'` so multi-select questions skipped GT entirely. Even with `RETENTION_GAP_CONCEPTS` flagging "WAP Channels" + an exemplar at app.js:1417 teaching this exact fact, neither layer **enforced** it on output. **Two-layer fix**: **Layer A — generic stem-vs-answer-count guard** (`_stemNumericMatchesAnswerCount`). Tight regex `(?:\bWhich\s+\|\(\s*Choose\s+\|^\s*Choose\s+)(TWO\|THREE\|FOUR\|FIVE\|two\|three\|four\|five\|[2-5])\b` matches "Which TWO" / "(Choose TWO)" / "Choose TWO" patterns only — deliberately tight to avoid false-positives on prose like "Pick two factor authentication" (verbs `Identify`/`Pick` excluded). For multi-select: asserts `q.answers.length === expectedCount`. For MCQ: rejects outright (an MCQ stem demanding multiple is type-mismatched on its face). Pass-through for `order` / `cli-sim` / `topology`. **Layer B — multi-select GT facts** (`_multiSelectGroundTruthOk`). Locks the 2.4 GHz canonical fact: stem signal `non-overlapp` + `channel` + (`2.4 GHz` OR `Wi-Fi`/`wireless`/`802.11`/`wlan`) → marked answers must extract to exactly the set `{1, 6, 11}` (sorted-equality check on `Number.isFinite` channel numbers). If not, reject. Designed as a table — future canonical multi-select facts (WPA3 ciphers, CIA properties, etc.) join the same function with their own stem-detection regex + canonical answer set. Wired into `validateQuestions`: stem-numeric guard runs at the top of the per-question filter (works for all qTypes); multi-select GT runs in the multi-select branch alongside existing structural validity. **Validation-audit harness updated** to extract the 2 new helpers + the `_STEM_NUMBER_WORDS` const block — without that, the audit subprocess hits `ReferenceError` because `validateQuestions` calls helpers that aren't in the temp-stub bundle. Always required when a new helper joins the validator pipeline. **UAT**: **10 new v4.81.16 assertions** — 8 structural (2 helper-existence + 1 const-existence + 2 wiring + 1 canonical-fact literal + 1 regex coverage + 1 false-positive-avoidance regression guard ensuring `Identify`/`Pick` verbs are NOT in the regex), **2 vm-fixture behavioral tests** — (a) the user-reported bug case ("Which TWO" + 3 answers) returns false, while a correct "(Choose TWO)" + 2 answers returns true, a no-explicit-count multi-select returns true (pass-through), and a MCQ stem with "Which TWO" returns false (type-mismatch); (b) the GT check rejects the bug case ({1,6} only), accepts the canonical {1,6,11}, rejects a wrong-set ({1,6,9}), and passes through unrelated multi-selects (e.g. "Which TWO ports does FTP use" with answers {20,21}). Validation audit still 64.7% catch / 0% FP after the additions — the two new layers add new rejection paths without false-positive any of the 23 broken-corpus or curated-good fixtures. Total UAT: 4547 → **4557** passing. Playwright: **79/79** still green. Cache: `netplus-v4.81.16`. ~150 LOC across `app.js` + `tests/uat.js` + `tests/validation-audit.js`. **96th ship**. **Sunday's 11th ship** — first same-day bugfix follow-up of the day, surfaced by user dogfooding immediately after the v4.81.15 stale-topic ship landed. Pattern repeats `feedback_dogfooding_beats_scanners.md`: real use catches what scanners miss. Future canonical multi-select facts can extend `_multiSelectGroundTruthOk` without touching MCQ paths. |
| v4.81.15 | **🕒 Stale-topic surfacing — 4-layer rotation algorithm (user request)**. User dump: *"across the app, theres gotta be something that monitors which topics haven't been touched yet in a while during setting up mixed question or exam simulator. maybe some kind of algorithm that make sure the user is addressing some topics that haven't been seen in a long while."* Investigation confirmed the gap: `computeWeakSpotScores()` already calculates per-topic staleness for the homepage Weak Spots widget, but that signal never feeds back into the question generator. `RETENTION_GAP_CONCEPTS` (v4.62.3) covers MISSED concepts as a soft tiebreaker, but not STALE (untouched) topics. After brainstorm, user picked **Layers 1+2+3+5** (deferred Layers 4 calendar-aware + 6 exam-coverage tracking as separate considerations). **(1) Base stale-topic injection** — new `_computeStaleTopics(historyRows, n, sliceIdx, sliceSize)` helper walks `TOPIC_DOMAINS` (50 topics) and combines `computeWeakSpotScores`'s posterior accuracy + `loadHistory`'s last-seen timestamps. Topics not seen in `WEAK_STALENESS_DAYS` (14d) become eligible; never-studied topics are infinitely stale (9999d sentinel). `_formatStaleTopicsForPrompt(staleTopics)` mirrors `_formatRetentionConceptsForPrompt`'s soft-preference framing: *"ROTATION PRIORITY: stay within the blueprint weights, but bias topic selection within each domain toward this list when reasonable"* — never a mandate. Injected after `${retentionBlock}` in `_fetchQuestionsBatch`'s `buildPrompt` template. Gated to MIXED_TOPIC only (single-topic + multi-topic quizzes already focus the user's explicit selection). **(2) Compound priority (the smart-rotation amplifier)** — `priority = daysSince × (1 + accGap)` where `accGap = max(0, WEAK_TARGET_ACC − posterior)`. A topic last seen 21d ago at 50% accuracy outranks one last seen 28d ago at 90% accuracy: B has more raw stale days, but A has more learning value to reclaim. Verified by vm fixture (`A_StaleAndWeak` 21d/50% MUST outrank `B_StaleButStrong` 28d/90% on priority — passes deterministically). **(3) Per-batch slice rotation (the exam-breadth amplifier)** — `_computeStaleTopics(history, n, sliceIdx, sliceSize)` returns a rotating window with step = `floor(sliceSize/2)` (50% overlap between consecutive slices for coverage continuity). `fetchQuestions` accepts an optional 5th parameter `staleSliceIdx` and threads it through to `_fetchQuestionsBatch`. `startExam` passes `i` (0..4) for each of the 5 sequential exam batches → each batch sees a *different* rotating window of stale topics, systematically covering MORE stale ground across a 90-Q exam instead of all 5 batches clustering at the same top-N. Marathon mode's batch loop also passes `i` for the same effect on bulk30/45/60. Within a single `fetchQuestions` parallel-batch case, sub-batches get `outerIdx + i` so even concurrent sub-batches see overlapping but non-identical windows. Retry-to-fill threads the same staleSliceIdx as the parent batch (so we keep filling the same rotation window). **(5) Homepage "Due for rotation" chip row** — closes the UX loop so the user can SEE the algorithm working. New `#rotation-row` element directly below `#todays-focus` (Weak Spots) on the home page. `renderRotationChips()` renders amber-tinted chips (visually distinct from accent-tinted Weak Spots — softer "FYI" treatment vs. urgent weak-spots) with topic name + meta strip ("21d stale · ~55% acc" or "never studied"). Click-to-drill via existing `focusTopic()`. Hidden when `loadHistory().length < STALE_CHIP_MIN_HISTORY` (5) so new users don't see a row of 50 stale topics they haven't studied yet — give the baseline time to build. Same dual-wiring discipline as v4.81.1: rendered from BOTH `goSetup()` (post-navigation refreshes) AND `DOMContentLoaded` (initial paint) so the chip row state is consistent on raw reload. **4 new constants**: `STALE_PROMPT_TOPIC_COUNT = 10` (injected per batch), `STALE_PROMPT_SLICE_SIZE = 10` (rotation window), `STALE_CHIP_TOPIC_COUNT = 5` (homepage), `STALE_CHIP_MIN_HISTORY = 5` (gate for both prompt + chip row). **Why this bundle**: #1 + #2 are the algorithmic core (without #2 it's a dumb timer; without #1 nothing has anything to bias). #3 unlocks exam breadth which is where the dogfood signal originated. #5 makes the invisible visible — same pattern as v4.81.13's domain breakdown card. Layers #4 (calendar-aware threshold tightening) and #6 (exam-coverage tracking) deferred as speculative without dogfood telemetry. **UAT**: **33 new v4.81.15 assertions** — 7 helper/constant existence (3 fns + 4 constants), 7 wiring (signature changes + propagation through fetchQuestions + _fetchQuestionsBatch + startExam main + retry + Marathon + parallel sub-batches), 5 prompt content (compound priority formula + ROTATION PRIORITY framing + blueprint-weight discipline + MIXED_TOPIC gate + STALE_CHIP_MIN_HISTORY gate + 9999 never-studied sentinel + reuses computeWeakSpotScores), 4 UI structural (HTML element + is-hidden default + .rotation-row + .rot-chip CSS + reduced-motion gate), 4 lifecycle wiring (renderRotationChips in goSetup + DOMContentLoaded), **3 vm-fixture behavioral tests** — (a) compound priority correctly ranks stale+weak above stale+mastered using deterministic stub `computeWeakSpotScores` (A_StaleAndWeak 21d/50% beats B_StaleButStrong 28d/90% by priority despite fewer raw stale days; D_NeverStudied wins overall on 9999-day staleness; C_Fresh < 14d filtered out), (b) slice rotation produces distinct windows across batches (sliceIdx 0 = T1..T4, sliceIdx 1 = T5..T8, sliceIdx 2 wraps modular back to T1..T4 — proves both rotation + wrap), (c) prompt formatter handles never-studied vs stale-with-history distinctly (never-studied uses sentinel string, doesn't leak the 9999d number into the prompt). Plus 6 existing structural-regex widenings to accept the new optional `staleSliceIdx` parameter (APP_VERSION + 5 fetchQuestions/startExam/Marathon callsites). Total UAT: 4514 → **4547** passing. Playwright: **79/79** still green. Cache: `netplus-v4.81.15`. ~330 LOC across `app.js` (helper + format + render fn + 5 callsite threadings) + `index.html` (1 element) + `styles.css` (1 chip-row block) + `tests/uat.js` (33 assertions). **95th ship**. **Sunday's 10th ship**. Closes the long-standing "no rotation algorithm" gap — the system now systematically surfaces stale-AND-weak topics into mixed quizzes + exam batches via prompt injection AND tells the user about it via a visible chip row. Layers 4 (calendar-aware) and 6 (exam-coverage tracking) remain on standby until dogfood telemetry justifies. |
| v4.81.14 | **🔁 Cross-batch question dedup (user-reported repeats)**. User report: *"some questions kept repeating themselves lol... in the exam simulator. also this happens in regular quizzes sometimes too but i noticed it a lot more in the exam simulator."* Investigation confirmed zero dedup anywhere in the question-fetch pipeline. Two failure modes: (1) `fetchQuestions` for n>10 splits into parallel `_fetchQuestionsBatch` calls via `Promise.allSettled` — concurrent batches can't see each other's output, so Haiku produces overlapping stems independently. (2) `startExam` calls `fetchQuestions` 5 times sequentially with no cross-call dedup; Haiku has no state from prior batches. **Fix**: stem-normalize-and-dedupe at two levels. **`_normalizeStemForDedup(stem)`**: lowercase + strip punctuation (`/[^\\w\\s]/g`) + collapse whitespace + 200-char cap. Catches *"Which of the following BEST describes ARP?"* and *"which of the following best describes arp."* as the same stem. **`fetchQuestions` parallel-batch merge**: Set-based first-seen-wins dedup as the merge step iterates `Promise.allSettled` results. Logs `deduped` count via `console.info` when > 0. **`startExam` per-batch loop**: before each batch concats into `examQuestions`, filter out any stem already in the running set. Plus the retry-to-fill payload also gets deduped (using a fresh seen-stem Set built from `examQuestions` + the current batch's already-deduped contents) — otherwise the retry would undo the dedup. Order matters: dedup happens BEFORE the existing retry-to-fill logic, so deficits from dropped duplicates auto-trigger a refill. No new failure modes — the existing DROPOUT_BUFFER + retry-to-fill cascade handles the shortfall. **UAT**: **8 new v4.81.14 assertions** — 1 helper exists + 1 helper logic check + 2 fetchQuestions wiring (Set + helper used; deduped count logged) + 2 startExam wiring (cross-call dedup against examQuestions; retry-to-fill uses seenStemsRetry too) + **2 vm-fixture behavioral tests** (normalization collapses case/punct/whitespace/nullish to same key; merge logic across 3 parallel batches with 2 deliberate overlaps verifies first-seen-wins keeps original case + drops duplicates). Total UAT: 4506 → **4514** passing. Playwright: **79/79** still green. Cache: `netplus-v4.81.14`. ~110 LOC across `app.js` + `tests/uat.js`. **94th ship**. **Sunday's 9th ship**. Closes the question-repetition gap that affected exam mode most heavily (5 sequential batches × 18 Qs = 90 chances for cross-batch overlap) but also occasionally surfaced in larger regular quizzes. |
