Audit found: Subnet Trainer's core pedagogy is strong (21 question types, adaptive difficulty, step-by-step feedback) but its dashboard was thin and nothing linked back into the main app's weak-spots loop. Topology Builder is ambitious (~4500 LOC, 65 labs, full L2/L3 sim) but the AI Coach was context-blind (generic "nice design" output regardless of whether the user was mid-lab), the lab inventory inflated "30 concept labs + 35 auto-generated variants" into a misleading flat "65 labs" count, and the UI was cluttered (wall-of-text intro banner, ungrouped toolbar with 12+ buttons and only visual dividers, weak empty-state). Fixed all of that in one bundled release. **(1) AI Coach + lab context**: `tbCoachTopology()` now branches on `tbActiveLab`. When a lab is active, the prompt is rewritten to say *"STUDENT IS ON STEP 3 OF 7: [title]. Step goal: [instruction]. Step hint: [hint]. CURRENT TOPOLOGY STATE: [serialized]."* — Claude responds as a tutor referencing the exact step, not a generic reviewer. Cache key differentiated by lab+step so returning to the same step is a cache hit but advancing fetches fresh coaching. Coach modal gets a new `.tb-coach-lab-badge` header showing "🧪 Lab: [title] · Step N of M" when active. Free-build mode falls back to v4.21.0 scenario-based prompt. ~60 lines touched, huge UX delta. **(2) Subnet Trainer dashboard callouts**: `stRenderDashboard` now shows three new prescriptive callouts pinned at the top before the existing category cards — **Weakest Categories** (accuracy <75% with ≥5 attempts, sorted ascending, top 3), **Stale Categories** (lastSeen >7 days ago, top 3), **Weakest Question Types** (the 21 granular types with accuracy <70% and ≥3 attempts). Each weak/stale row is a click-through to `stDashJumpToCategory(catId)` which auto-switches to Practice tab + Focus mode + pre-selects the category. Turns the dashboard from "bare stats" into "here's what to drill right now, in one tap." **(3) Weak-spots → Subnet Trainer bridge (minimal)**: new `WEAK_SPOT_DRILL_BRIDGES` map routes three subnetting-related weak topics (`Subnetting & IP Addressing`, `IPv6`, `NAT & IP Services`) to the Subnet Trainer. `renderTodaysFocus` checks the current weak topics against the map; if any match, a small dashed-border "🧮 Drill in Subnet Trainer →" pill appears below the weak-spots chip row. Deduped by destination so users don't see the same link twice. Deliberately excludes Topology Builder from the bridge per user direction — topology is a standalone self-directed activity, not a reactive drill target. **(4) Topology Builder UI polish**: replaced the `<details>` collapsible intro with a compact `.tb-hero` card — one-line value prop + 5 feature pills (Design / Simulate / 29 concept labs / AI Coach + Generate / Export PNG). Toolbar redesigned from flat row with 5 divider spans to grouped layout (`.tb-toolbar-v2` with 6 `.tb-tool-group` sections: Primary actions · Simulate · Practice · File · Scenario · Utility), each group has a small uppercase label above the buttons for scanability. Empty-state upgraded from "drag a device" one-liner to a proper first-run panel with 3 large CTA tiles (Start a guided lab / AI Generate / Fix a broken network) — gives first-time users a clear way in beyond blank-canvas. Lab picker regrouped via new `TB_LAB_CATEGORIES` map (Fundamentals / Switching / Routing / Services / Security / Cloud & WAN / Wireless & QoS / Troubleshooting) with honest counts: shows "29 concept labs + 35 auto-generated configs" instead of the inflated "65 labs" claim. Auto-generated variants (previously cryptic IDs like `c_auto_1`, `d_vpnlab_dc2`) are now collapsed under a dashed-border "Auto-generated configs" section and relabeled as "Config A/B/C/D" so users understand they're practicing the same concept with different inputs. **(5) Two new troubleshooting labs**: added `troubleshoot-vlan-isolation` (Intermediate, obj 5.3 — Sales/HR VLAN misconfig where PC2's switch port is accidentally in VLAN 20 instead of 10, student navigates Interfaces tab to fix) and `troubleshoot-dhcp-relay` (Intermediate, obj 3.4 — PCs in subnet B can't get IPs from DHCP server in subnet A because the router has no helper-address configured, student adds DHCP relay on R1's subnet-B-facing interface). Both labs follow the existing `troubleshoot-connectivity` pattern: `autoSetup()` builds the broken topology, per-step `check(state)` validates the fix as the student makes it, `feedback(state)` explains what's still missing with specific next actions. Troubleshooting domain coverage went from 1 lab (`troubleshoot-connectivity` covered routing issues) to 3 — now VLAN-level and service-level troubleshooting both have dedicated scaffolded diagnosis labs. Both added to `TB_LAB_CATEGORIES.Troubleshooting`. **UAT**: 90 new v4.43.1 assertions across all 5 items. Also updated 8 pre-existing v4.34 topology-builder UI assertions that were locking the old `<details>`-based intro / `tb-toolbar-divider` / `tb-toolbar-spacer` shapes — rewrote them to match the new grouped layout while preserving the regression-guard intent. Total UAT: 2412 → **2458** passing. Validation-audit regression gate still green. Cache bumped to `netplus-v4.43.1`. |
| v4.43.0 | **Keyword highlighting in question stems** — new product feature (minor version bump, not maintenance). CompTIA exam stems use specific trap words that change meaning: *"Which of the following is NOT..."*, *"MOST secure option EXCEPT for..."*, *"The FIRST step in the troubleshooting methodology..."*. Missing these words is the #2 wrong-answer mode after "I didn't know it" — test-takers skim and miss the negation or superlative. This release auto-highlights them at render time to train the eye to catch them on the real exam. **14-keyword dictionary**: `NOT`, `EXCEPT`, `CANNOT` (negation), `MOST`, `LEAST`, `BEST`, `WORST`, `PRIMARY` (superlatives), `FIRST`, `LAST`, `NEXT` (sequence), `ALWAYS`, `NEVER`, `ONLY` (absolutes). Deliberately **excludes** `all`, `none`, `any`, `could`, `should`, `would`, `which` — those are too common in plain prose, would produce visual noise. UAT regression-guards the exclusion list. **Rendering approach**: new `setQuestionText(el, raw)` helper that does `el.innerHTML = highlightExamKeywords(escHtml(raw))` — single entry point for all 5 render paths (quiz stem, exam stem, review page, CLI sim scenario, topology scenario). Escapes HTML first (XSS-safe since `q.question` is AI-generated), then wraps keywords in `<strong class="exam-keyword">`. Word-boundary regex with `gi` flags so case is preserved (lowercase "not" in prose stays lowercase but still styled — doesn't visually conflict since the styling is background + color, not text-transform). **CSS**: subtle chip styling — bold + accent-light color + 10% accent background + inset bottom-border underline. Light theme gets a slightly darker accent variant for contrast. NOT a big shout — keywords should catch the eye without dominating the sentence. **What's NOT touched**: Explain Further content, Topic Deep Dive, Topic Brief, Analytics pages — those are teacher-generated content, not questions. Keywords only appear in question stems where the pedagogy win lives. **UAT**: 44 new v4.43.0 assertions — constants/helpers present, all 14 keywords covered, 7 ambiguous words explicitly excluded, 5 render paths wired up, 2 regression guards against old `textContent`-based rendering, 3 CSS presence checks, 2 XSS-safety guards (escape before highlight, null-input handling), and a 7-case behavioral smoke test that verifies upper-case / mixed-case / multiple-keywords / plain-prose / word-boundary / excluded-word / escaped-HTML-entity behavior all work correctly. Total UAT: 2368 → **2412** passing. Validation-audit regression gate still green. Cache bumped to `netplus-v4.43.0`. |
| v4.42.5 | **Maintenance bundle — 4 tech-debt issues closed in one release** — targeted Friday tech-debt ship after the 2026-04-16 sweep (#140) flagged hot-churn items compounding on files with 44 commits/30d. Picked the 4 highest-value non-SaaS-gated items and shipped as a single bundled release to minimize deploy churn. **#130 — Magic numbers extracted**: added 11 named constants at the top of app.js replacing bare literals scattered across the codebase. `EXAM_PASS_SCORE = 720` (CompTIA official pass threshold, replacing 8 hardcoded behavioral comparisons), `EXAM_QUESTION_COUNT = 90`, `EXAM_MAX_SCORE = 900`, `DOUBLE_CLICK_MS = 400` (topology canvas double-click detection), `VXLAN_VNI_MAX = 16777215` (24-bit VNI range per RFC 7348), plus 6 `MAX_TOKENS_*` constants for the AI call sites (generation / validation / teacher-default / teacher-long / teacher-coach / teacher-brief — replaces 9 bare `max_tokens:` literals that had drifted into various call shapes). Behavioral comparisons against 720 (pass score) and hardcoded max_tokens were the ones most likely to keep sneaking in via new AI call sites, which was the compounding-debt signal. UAT has a regression guard `!/max_tokens:\s*\d+/.test(js)` that fails loud if bare literals reappear. **#72 — openGuidedLab whitelist trap removed**: the v4.16.2 bug (Back button from Guided Lab dumping users on a stale Topic Deep Dive) was caused by a hardcoded whitelist `['page-topic-dive', 'page-ports', 'page-quiz', ...]` that silently fell back to 'page-ports' if the currently-active page wasn't listed. Every new page added after the whitelist was frozen could trip it. Replaced with `document.querySelector('.page.active')` which works for any page regardless of ID. Added a belt-and-braces guard against capturing `page-guided-lab` as the return target itself (edge case where openGuidedLab is called from within the lab page). Defensive fallback to 'page-ports' preserved. Regression guards ensure the old whitelist array can't silently reappear. **#128 — Drill accessibility pass**: the 3 newer drill pages (Acronym Blitz, OSI Sorter, Cable & Connector ID) had minimal ARIA coverage vs the quiz/exam pages. Added across all three: `aria-label` on tablists, `aria-selected` + `aria-controls` on tab buttons, `role="tabpanel"` + `aria-labelledby` on tab panels, `tabindex` management (0 on active tab/panel, -1 on inactive) for keyboard navigation, `aria-pressed` on mode toggle buttons + OSI difficulty buttons, `aria-live="polite"` + `aria-atomic="true"` on the score/streak stats strips so screen readers announce score changes without re-reading the entire label, and `aria-live="polite"` on the question card containers. The shared `createDrillScaffold.setTab()` and `setMode()` helpers were updated to sync `aria-selected` + `aria-pressed` states alongside the existing `.active` class toggles — so the a11y state stays in sync automatically across all 3 drills without per-drill duplication. `setOsDifficulty` got the same treatment for difficulty buttons. Out of scope for this pass: OSI drag-and-drop keyboard fallback (bigger change, separate ticket). **#141 — evaluateMilestones table-driven refactor**: the 151-line function with 29 `maybe(id, cond)` calls interleaved with context-building logic was the biggest single milestone-eval function in the codebase and #1 of the 24-offender long-function CI breach (target: 22). Refactored into three pieces: `_buildMilestoneCtx()` (gathers all 47 milestone context data once — history, exam stats, readiness, streak, subnet/port/drill stats, day-of-week/time-of-day bookkeeping, lab/AB/OS/CB/fix mastery with defensive try/catch around optional APIs), `MILESTONE_CHECKS` (a 47-entry declarative table of `{ id, check: (ctx) => boolean }` one-liners — every milestone is now one line), and `evaluateMilestones()` itself which becomes a 10-line tight loop that iterates the table, calls `unlockMilestone(id)` on matching checks, and returns newly-unlocked IDs. Also extracted `_scaledExamScore(e)` helper (the CompTIA 100-900 scaling formula shared by `exam_pass` + `hardcore_pass`). Adding a new milestone is now one line in the `MILESTONE_CHECKS` table instead of mixing into the context-gathering. Per-check `try/catch` preserved so a single broken check can't kill the whole eval. UAT has regression guards for all 47 milestone IDs (if any go missing, UAT fails loud) plus body-length + table-pattern + helper-extraction assertions. **UAT**: 98 new v4.42.5 assertions across all 4 fixes. The 24→23 function-count reduction from the #141 refactor brings the CI breach within 1 of the threshold. |
| v4.42.4 | **Readiness algorithm — within-domain question-count weighting fix** — user asked for a correctness audit of the exam readiness calculator. Audit surfaced one real flaw and three deferrable tuning preferences. Shipped the correctness fix; filed the rest on Board #1 gated on SaaS-pivot user data. **The flaw**: `getReadinessScore()` was computing domain accuracy as the simple average of per-topic percentages (`pctSum / count`), giving equal weight to a topic with 2 questions and one with 200. The real CompTIA exam weights every question equally — so a user who is 95% on OSPF (20 weighted Q's) and 50% on BGP (4 weighted Q's) has a real-exam-equivalent implementation accuracy of `(19+2)/(20+4) = 87.5%`, not the simple average of 72.5%. The v4.42.3 catalog expansion (40 → 50 topics) made the flaw more visible because new child topics start with 0 questions while parent umbrellas have many — high topic-count variance makes the averaging distortion bigger. **The fix**: ~10 lines in `getReadinessScore()`. Swap `pctSum += pct; count++` aggregation for `wCorrect += topicMap[t].wCorrect; wTotal += topicMap[t].wTotal` — then domain average is `wCorrect / wTotal * 100` across all topics in the domain, properly weighted by question count. Unstudied-domain behavior preserved (still computes 0 and drags the score down). The 40/25/20/15 signal weights (accuracy / coverage / recency / volume), 420-870 scaling, domain weights (23/20/19/14/24), difficulty multipliers (Hard 2.0 / Exam 1.5 / Found 1.0), exam-mode boost 1.3×, 7-day recency boost 2×, 14-day recency decay window, and 500-Q volume cap are all **untouched** — those were reviewed and deemed correct. **Deferred tuning opportunities** (filed as issue #139, gated on SaaS-pivot user data): (1) Recency denominator is `totalTopics` not `studiedTopics`, which subtly makes recency signal partially a coverage signal, redundant with the Coverage signal itself; (2) No PBQ weighting in accuracy calc — real CompTIA exam weights PBQs heavier than MCQs, but the algorithm treats them the same; (3) Triple-penalty for low coverage (coverage × 0.5 under 5 topics, unstudied domains = 0 accuracy, small recency numerator) — mathematically fair but potentially discouraging for early users. Each of these is a judgment call without clear "right" answer for a single-user tool; revisit when SaaS has real user data to observe what correlates with pass rates. **UAT**: 10 new v4.42.4 assertions — 5 structural regression guards (new `wCorrect/wTotal` aggregation present, old `pctSum/count` pattern gone, `bucket.wTotal > 0` division-by-zero guard) + 5 behavioral smoke assertions on a synthetic fixture that proves (a) new logic gives 87.5% on unequal-Q-count data, (b) old logic would have given 72.5%, (c) new vs old differ by >10% when Q counts vary, (d) new and old agree when Q counts are equal (shows the fix is a strict upgrade, not a swap), (e) unstudied domain still returns 0. Total UAT: 2260 → **2270** passing. Cache bumped to `netplus-v4.42.4`. |

| v4.42.1 | **Landing-page intro animation — fill-from-empty reveal on Readiness + Daily Goal** — follow-up focused animation patch after v4.42.0's big 8-fix pass. User posted a screenshot of the setup page and asked: *"What would be a cool animation is when i land on the page, the exam readiness and daily goal circle have a cool load up animation"*. | v4.42.0 | **Animation pass — celebration toasts + milestone unlocks + motion hardening** — eight fixes shipped together after an audit of the homepage/results animation story flagged real gaps. User scope was explicit: *"do all the fixes today aswell as the 3 you were suggesting to defer. i want them all done for V4.42.0"*. **(1) Readiness score roll-up**: `renderReadinessCard()` used to hot-swap `numEl.textContent = predicted` which wiped the old value instantly. Now reads `parseInt(numEl.textContent, 10)` as the previous value and calls the existing `animateCount('readiness-num', oldVal, predicted, 900)` helper when they differ — the 900ms cubic-ease-out count-up makes the score visibly climb (e.g. 612 → 647) after a quiz. Falls back to direct assignment on first render (NaN old value). **(2) Homepage-card refresh hooks in finish() / submitExam()**: pre-v4.42 the setup-page cards (`renderStatsCard`, `renderReadinessCard`) were only refreshed when the user navigated back via `goSetup()` — so the next goSetup render showed stale data for a split second before recomputing. Both finish/submitExam now call `renderStatsCard()` and `renderReadinessCard()` directly after `saveToHistory()`, so by the time the user hits Back the DOM already reflects the new history row. **(3) Milestone celebration toast + (4) evaluateMilestones return capture**: discovered a pre-existing architectural bug — `evaluateMilestones()` was NEVER called from `finish()` or `submitExam()`, milestones only unlocked lazily when the user happened to open the Analytics page. Big ones like `first_quiz`, `hundred_qs`, `perfect_quiz`, `first_exam`, `exam_pass`, `hardcore_pass`, `streak_7`, `streak_30` would silently accrue in localStorage but never celebrate. Now `evaluateMilestones()` is called at the end of both finish() and submitExam(), the returned `newlyUnlocked` array is captured, and each unlock fires a staggered `showMilestoneCelebration(id)` call (500ms + 900ms per milestone in finish; 900ms base in submitExam so it doesn't collide with the exam-pass confetti). New helpers: `showMilestoneCelebration(id)` reads `MILESTONE_DEFS` to find the icon/label/desc, calls `showCelebrationToast(icon+label, desc)` + `launchMiniConfetti()`. `showCelebrationToast(titleText, subText)` clones the `showErrorToast` DOM-append pattern but with a distinct purple/gold gradient palette and a 3800ms display window. **(5) @media (prefers-reduced-motion: reduce) gate**: audit found zero accessibility coverage for motion-sensitive users. Added a global block to styles.css that neutralizes `.celebration-toast` transitions (.01ms linear), kills `.streak-pulse` animations (`animation: none`), strips transform transitions from `.tf-chip`, and reduces `.dg-ring-fill` + `.grade-fill` stroke-dashoffset transitions to .01ms so the final state is still painted without visible motion. **(6) Streak pulse on increment**: new module-level `_pendingStreakPulse` flag set in finish/submitExam when `getStreak().current > _prevStreakBefore` (snapshot captured before `updateStreak()`). `renderStreakBadge()` consumes the flag in `goSetup()`, adds a `.streak-pulse` class that triggers a 900ms `@keyframes streakPulse` (scale 1→1.12→1 with an orange `box-shadow: 0 0 0 10px rgba(251,146,60,0)` ripple), and cleans up via `animationend`. Flag is set while the setup page is hidden (during results) and consumed when setup becomes visible, so the user sees the pulse *on arrival* at the homepage, not during the quiz. **(7) Weak Spots FLIP rerank animation**: `renderTodaysFocus()` now uses First-Last-Invert-Play. Captures `getBoundingClientRect()` of each existing `.tf-chip[data-topic]` into an `oldRects` map BEFORE the innerHTML rewrite, stamps `data-topic` on new chips so lookup keys match, then iterates the new chips post-rewrite: for each one that existed before, computes `dx/dy` deltas between old and new positions, applies `translate(dx,dy)` + `transition: none`, forces a reflow via `void el.offsetWidth`, then releases by setting `transition: transform 420ms cubic-bezier(0.2, 0.8, 0.2, 1)` and clearing the transform. Chip appears to glide from old slot to new. **Critical supporting change**: finish() and submitExam() no longer call `renderTodaysFocus()` directly (the v4.38.7 defensive calls). The double-render was defeating FLIP — first call happened while `#page-setup` was hidden (all bounding rects 0), second call measured the already-updated DOM with no diff detected. Moving the single call to `goSetup()` alone gives FLIP a real old → new delta to animate. UAT has regression guards (`finish() no longer calls renderTodaysFocus (FLIP guard)`) so a future refactor can't silently reintroduce the double-render. **(8) Mini confetti variant**: `launchMiniConfetti()` is a subtler cousin of `launchConfetti()` — 40 particles (vs 150), 80 frames (vs 200), 5-color gold/accent palette (`#fbbf24`, `#f59e0b`, `#fde047`, `#7c6ff7`, `#22c55e`) vs the 8-color rainbow, origin point at `(canvas.width/2, 80)` (near the top where the celebration toast lives) vs randomized across the screen, radial emission pattern (angle = `2π * i / count + jitter`) vs falling-from-top. Subtler celebration for milestone unlocks without stealing thunder from the big exam-pass burst. **UAT**: 42 new v4.42.0 assertions verify every piece — readiness roll-up wiring, celebration toast DOM lifecycle, `showMilestoneCelebration` reading `MILESTONE_DEFS`, evaluateMilestones return capture in both finish and submitExam, FLIP rerank (data-topic stamping, `oldRects` capture, inverse transform application, transitionend cleanup), streak-pulse flag lifecycle (declared, set in finish/submitExam, consumed in renderStreakBadge, CSS `@keyframes streakPulse`), mini-confetti particle count + palette separation, `@media (prefers-reduced-motion: reduce)` block presence, and FLIP guards preventing future regressions of the finish/submitExam → renderTodaysFocus double-render. Total UAT: 2126 → **2168** passing. Validation-audit regression gate still green. Cache bumped to `netplus-v4.42.0`. |

| v4.39.0 | **Topology Builder — bigger canvas + force-directed auto-layout for AI-generated topologies** — user posted a screenshot of a "standard school network" generated via the topology builder's AI Generate, devices were all bunched in the upper-left quadrant of the canvas: *"the network as you can see it totally bunched together which is not very appealing. i need the topolgiies generated to be perfectly spaced out across the canvas. (2) **New `tbAutoLayout(state)` force-directed function** — runs unconditionally inside `tbDeepValidateAndFix` after AI generation, replacing the old "stacked-at-(400,400)" detector that only caught devices stuck at exact defaults and missed Haiku's gently-bunched output. Algorithm: detects clustered seeds (max-min spread < 250px on either axis) and grid-seeds them across the canvas first, then runs 260 iterations of a force-directed simulation with pair-wise repulsion (`REPULSE = 9000 / dist²`), cable-based spring attraction (`SPRING = 0.06`, `IDEAL_LINK = 200`), velocity damping (0.85), velocity cap (30), and bounds clamping with 100×90 padding. Final hard-separation pass (up to 30 iterations) guarantees no two devices closer than `MIN_SEP = 150` regardless of what the simulation converged to. Returns count of devices that moved more than 8px so `tbDeepValidateAndFix` can append "Auto-layout repositioned N device(s) for clarity" to the user-facing fix list. (3) **AI prompt updated** to mention the new 1800×1100 canvas, the 150-1650 / 120-980 spread range, and the 180px minimum spacing rule — with a note that positions get auto-relayouted post-generation, so if Haiku ignores the instruction (which it often does), the deterministic post-pass still fixes it. (4) **9 new UAT assertions** covering function presence, constant + parameter wiring, the `tbDeepValidateAndFix` call site, the AI-prompt updates, and a behavioral smoke test that extracts `tbAutoLayout` into a Function() sandbox, feeds it 8 devices stacked at (400,400) ±5px, and asserts the post-layout min pair distance is ≥140px. Live-preview verification: `tbAutoLayout` was fed a 10-device topology mimicking the user's screenshot (firewall → IDS → router → LB → switch → 3 PCs + 2 servers + printer, all clustered around 500,470), and the function spread them across x:455–1700, y:90–859 with min pair distance 195px. | v4.38.7 | **Weak Spots v2 — robust, real-time ranking algorithm** — user posted a screenshot of the front-page "🎯 Weak spots" chip row and asked for "a more robust and deeper calculation algorithm for what my weak spots are and they need to update in real time." The old `getTodaysFocusTopics()` was a 15-line heuristic: +2 per wrong-bank entry + a flat `(0.75 - accuracy) * 20` bonus for topics under 75% history accuracy. Eight weaknesses: no recency decay (a 3-month-old wrong counted the same as a 1-hour-old wrong), no confidence interval (one bad 5-Q run instantly dominated), no difficulty weighting, no domain importance, no staleness for topics you studied once and forgot, no hooks into quiz-completion paths for real-time updates, and it lumped untouched topics (no signal) in with weak topics (bad signal). Rewrote as `computeWeakSpotScores()` — a proper scoring model that combines four signals: (1) **recency-decayed wrong-bank count** — exponential decay with 7-day half-life (`WEAK_HALF_LIFE_WRONGS_MS = 7 * 86400000`), difficulty-weighted via the existing `diffWeight()` helper (Hard 2.0× / Exam 1.5× / Foundational 1.0×), half-credit for entries where `rightCount >= 1` since they're already partially graduated. A wrong from yesterday counts ~0.9, a wrong from 14 days ago counts ~0.25, a wrong from 60 days ago counts ~0.003 — old mistakes fade. (2) **Bayesian posterior accuracy gap** — recency-decayed weighted correct/total from `loadHistory()` (14-day half-life via `WEAK_HALF_LIFE_HIST_MS`, exam-mode boost 1.3×, difficulty-weighted). Raw accuracy is smoothed with a Beta(2,2) prior: `posterior = (wCorrect + 2) / (wTotal + 4)`. This means a single bad 3/5 run doesn't instantly flag the topic as weak — the prior acts like 2 phantom correct + 2 phantom wrong answers, so the posterior only moves meaningfully once you've built real volume. Gap = `max(0, 0.85 - posterior)` against the `WEAK_TARGET_ACC = 0.85` mastery threshold. (3) **Staleness bonus** — topics untouched for more than `WEAK_STALENESS_DAYS = 14` days start accruing up to a `WEAK_STALENESS_CAP = 2.0` multiplier, so a topic you once mastered but haven't revisited in 6 weeks doesn't fade off the radar entirely. Computed as `(daysSince - 14) / 14`, capped. (4) **Domain importance multiplier** — `_weakDomainMultiplier(topic)` reads `TOPIC_DOMAINS[topic]` and returns `DOMAIN_WEIGHTS[dom] / 0.2` (average of the 5 weights), so a weak Troubleshooting topic (24%) outranks a weak Security topic (14%) at equal raw badness — matches the real N10-009 domain distribution. Range is ~0.7× (security) to ~1.2× (troubleshooting). Final score = `(wrongsRecent * 3.0 + accGap * 25.0 + staleness * 2.0) * domainMul`. **Low-signal filter**: topics with `wTotal < 1 && wrongsRecent < 0.5` are excluded — that's "untouched, not weak" (the Study Plan card handles coverage). **Backward compat**: `getTodaysFocusTopics(limit)` is now a 1-line wrapper around `computeWeakSpotScores().slice(0, limit).map(r => r.topic)` so the existing callers (Focused preset on the setup page, weakest-topic fallback in `applyPreset`) still work unchanged. **Real-time hooks**: `renderTodaysFocus()` now shows a tooltip per chip with the computed posterior accuracy, recent-wrongs count, and staleness-in-days — so you can hover/tap a chip and see *why* it's flagged. Added `renderTodaysFocus()` calls directly into `finish()` and `submitExam()` after the `saveToHistory()` line, so every quiz and exam completion refreshes the chips immediately (goSetup already called it on back-navigation; these new calls cover direct page-switch paths). **27 new UAT assertions** verify every piece: constant definitions (`WEAK_HALF_LIFE_*`, `WEAK_TARGET_ACC`, `WEAK_STALENESS_*`), helper definitions (`_weakDecay`, `_weakDomainMultiplier`), the Bayesian prior regex (`(wCorrect + 2) / (wTotal + 4)`), `diffWeight`/`_weakDomainMultiplier`/exam-boost usage inside the function body, descending sort, low-signal exclusion guard, graduation half-credit logic, the `finish()` + `submitExam()` refresh hooks, and `renderTodaysFocus()` displaying the posterior in its tooltip. One assertion is a **behavioral smoke test**: extracts `computeWeakSpotScores` + `_weakDecay` + `_weakDomainMultiplier` + the constants into a sandbox, stubs `loadWrongBank`/`loadHistory`/`TOPIC_DOMAINS`/`DOMAIN_WEIGHTS`/`diffWeight`/`MIXED_TOPIC`/`EXAM_TOPIC`, runs the function against a synthetic fixture (3 recent wrongs on Troubleshooting + 1 recent wrong + moderate history on PKI + IPv6 history + a Mixed noise entry), and asserts: (a) non-empty results, (b) Mixed topic is excluded, (c) untouched-topic sentinel is excluded, (d) rows are sorted descending, (e) heavy-wrong Troubleshooting outranks lighter PKI, (f) Bayesian posterior is computed and in (0,1) for topics with history, (g) `wrongsRaw` display count is correct. Offline tests can't exercise real user behavior, but they CAN prove the algorithm produces the right ranking for the exact class of input the user's real wrong-bank will have. Total UAT: 2028 → **2059** passing. Validation-audit regression gate still green. Cache bumped to `netplus-v4.38.7`. |
| v4.38.6 | **Auto-negotiation vs Auto-MDIX ground truth — Ethernet physical layer hardening** — user hit a Haiku-generated Cabling & Topology MCQ whose stem asked about automatic MDI/MDIX pin detection on a too-long cable run but marked "Auto-negotiation, which automatically detects cable polarity and adjusts pin assignments" as the correct answer. This is a conflation: auto-negotiation (IEEE 802.3u clause 28) handles SPEED and DUPLEX only; Auto-MDIX (IEEE 802.3ab clause 40) is the distinct feature that detects MDI/MDIX pinout and swaps TX/RX. The two are bundled on modern gear which is why Haiku generates it wrong and Sonnet validation missed it — the v4.38.5 ground-truth tables (`GT_PORTS`, `GT_OSI`, `GT_WIFI_*`) had no Ethernet-physical-layer coverage. Belt-and-braces fix in two layers so the class of bug can't resurface: (1) **`GT_ETHERNET` truth table** — 6 entries covering auto-negotiation, auto-MDIX, MDI/MDIX, straight-through vs crossover, duplex mismatch, and PoE standards (802.3af/at/bt 15.4/30/60/100W). Each entry is a (feature, authoritative description) pair. Source comments cite the specific 802.3 clause so future refactors can't erode the facts. (2) **`_buildGtHint()` Ethernet branch** — new `ethRe` regex fires on any of `auto-negotiat`, `auto-mdix`, `mdix`, `mdi/mdix`, `crossover`, `straight-through`, `duplex`, `poe`, `poe+`, or any `802.3x` reference in the question text or topic name. When it matches, the helper unconditionally prepends both the auto-negotiation AND auto-MDIX facts to the AUTHORITATIVE FACTS block (surfacing the distinction even if only one is named in the stem), plus conditional duplex-mismatch and PoE-wattage facts on keyword match. This means every Tier A teacher call site (`explainFurther`, `showTopicDeepDive`, `fetchTopicBrief`) that gets an Ethernet-physical question now sees the two features spelled out as distinct before the Sonnet teacher model writes a word — no more conflation in deep dives, topic guides, or pre-quiz briefs. (3) **`_groundTruthOk()` programmatic guard** — new `mdiStemRe` detects question stems asking about MDI/MDIX, pin assignments, crossover, or straight-through cable auto-detection. If a stem matches AND the marked answer invokes auto-negotiation without also mentioning auto-MDIX, `_groundTruthOk()` returns false and `validateQuestions()` drops the question cold before it reaches the quiz UI. Reverse check with `speedDuplexStemRe`: if the stem is clearly about speed/duplex negotiation and the marked answer blames auto-MDIX, that's the inverse conflation — also dropped. This is the authoritative guard — even if the teacher prompt's GT injection somehow fails or gets bypassed, the programmatic validator in the quiz generation pipeline still catches the question. The user's exact bug (MDI/MDIX stem → auto-negotiation answer) now fails both layers. (4) **12 new UAT assertions** verify the constant exists, the regex is wired, both features are unconditionally surfaced on ethernet-keyword match, the AUTHORITATIVE FACTS header is emitted, and the `_groundTruthOk` guards are present. One assertion is a behavioral smoke test: it extracts `GT_ETHERNET` + `_buildGtHint` into a sandbox via `Function()`, calls the helper with a Cabling & Topology style MDI/MDIX stem, and asserts the returned string includes both "SPEED and DUPLEX only" and "pin assignments" — offline tests can't exercise real Claude output, but they CAN prove the helper emits the right facts for the exact scenario that broke. Total UAT: 2016 → **2028** passing. Validation-audit regression gate still green (62.5% catch rate, 0 false positives). Cache bumped to `netplus-v4.38.6`. |
| v4.38.5 | **AI teacher pipeline audit — Tier A/B/C hardening** — after v4.38.4 closed the quiz-question validation loop, a deeper audit surfaced 7 other Claude call sites that render content the user trusts as authoritative (explanations, topic guides, coach responses). Every one of them was still on Haiku 4.5 (same model that slipped 6/16 broken questions pre-fix) with no ground-truth checks and no caching. This release hardens all 7. (1) **New `CLAUDE_TEACHER_MODEL = 'claude-sonnet-4-6'` constant** separate from `CLAUDE_MODEL` (Haiku, generation) and `CLAUDE_VALIDATOR_MODEL` (Sonnet, validation). Three-way model split makes intent explicit. (2) **Tier A — authoritative study content (3 sites)**: `explainFurther()` (6-section deep dive shown after answer), `showTopicDeepDive()` / `buildTopicDivePrompt()` (full topic guide page), and `fetchTopicBrief()` (pre-quiz topic brief) all swapped to Sonnet. Re-opening the same deep dive or topic guide is now a free localStorage hit. (3) **Tier B — math must be exact (2 sites)**: `stAskCoach()` (subnet trainer explain-my-mistake) now computes the deterministic binary breakdown (IP / mask / IP-AND-mask network address) from the question's IP+CIDR and stuffs it into the prompt as "AUTHORITATIVE FACTS" before asking Sonnet for an explanation — the AI can't hallucinate the math when the answer is staring at it in the prompt. `ptAskCoach()` (port drill explain) now tags the correct `proto → port` as an "AUTHORITATIVE FACT (do not contradict)" line and swaps to Sonnet. (4) **Tier C — topology builder coaches (2 sites)**: `tbCoachTopology()` (student topology walkthrough) and `tbExplainDevice()` (single-device role explanation) both swapped to Sonnet. `tbGenerateAiTopology()` deliberately stays on Haiku because it's bulk JSON generation that already has `tbDeepValidateAndFix` as a post-pass — a Sonnet upgrade there would triple costs for minimal quality gain. `fetchQuestions()` also stays on Haiku for the same reason (validated by the Sonnet validator second pass). A helper `_fnBody(src, name)` walks brace depth to extract individual function bodies so the assertions scope to the right call site. Offline tests can't exercise AI output, but they CAN prove the hardening is wired — a refactor that silently reverts any of these fixes will now fail UAT. Total UAT: 1993 → **2016** passing. The validation-audit regression gate still runs in UAT; programmatic catch rate holds at 62.5% with 0 false positives. Cache bumped to `netplus-v4.38.5`. |
| v4.38.4 | **Question quality pipeline — deep audit + 5-fix upgrade** — after a user hit an explanation-answer mismatch bug (DC three-tier question: explanation correctly described "access tier contains servers and storage" but answer was marked as Core), ran a deep vulnerability audit of the 3-layer quality pipeline (generation prompt → AI validation pass → programmatic `validateQuestions`). Built `tests/validation-audit.js` — a 20-question broken-corpus regression fixture covering 16 distinct failure modes (premise-answer contradiction, explanation-answer mismatch, wrong port numbers, two valid answers, no correct answer, keyword overlap, WPA3 contradiction, short-option keyword blindness, outdated fact, stub explanation, subnet math error, missing/invalid objective, malformed answer letter, explicit wrong-letter claim, subjective qualifier GOOD, negation phrasing GOOD) plus 4 clean controls. Baseline v4.38.3 catch rate was **31.3% (5/16)**. Shipped 5 fixes: (1) **Unique-word scoring with negation guard** — `validateQuestions()` mcq branch now tokenizes each option minus stopwords, computes the distinctive token set per option via set subtraction, and scores each set against the explanation with a 40-char-before + 30-char-after negation-context window. If any distractor scores ≥1 AND beats the marked answer's score, the question is dropped. Only runs for non-negation questions (skips on NOT/EXCEPT/"which not"). (2) **Ground truth tables** — new `GT_PORTS` (27 protocol→port mappings), `GT_OSI` (30 protocol→layer), `GT_WIFI_BROKEN` (`['wep']`), `GT_WIFI_DEPRECATED` (`['wpa']`) static tables. `_groundTruthOk(q)` checks port-for-protocol questions, protocol-for-port questions, OSI layer questions, and wireless security questions against the tables — any deterministic N10-009 fact with a wrong answer gets rejected cold. (3) **Numeric-option path** — `_numericOptionOk(q)` detects questions where all 4 options are numeric (subnet math, port numbers, host counts) and scans the explanation for final-answer phrases (`leaves N`, `N usable`, `= N`, `total of N`, `results in N`) — if the phrase value doesn't match the marked answer's numeric value, the question is dropped. (4) **CI regression gate** — `tests/validation-audit.js` now enforces a `MIN_CATCH_RATE = 60` floor and `MAX_FP_RATE = 0` ceiling, exiting non-zero on breach. `tests/uat.js` spawns it via `execSync` as a new "Validation audit: regression gate" test, so a refactor to `validateQuestions()` can never silently regress below the known baseline and the UAT suite will fail loudly. (5) **Sonnet AI validator** — new `CLAUDE_VALIDATOR_MODEL = 'claude-sonnet-4-6'` constant alongside the existing Haiku `CLAUDE_MODEL`. `aiValidateQuestions()` now fires its second-pass semantic check against Sonnet instead of Haiku, because the remaining slips after fixes 1-3 are all deeper reasoning failures (premise-answer logical contradictions, "no correct answer" questions, two-valid-answer questions) that Haiku can't reliably catch. Generation stays on Haiku for cost/latency; validation trades a few cents per quiz for dramatically better semantic judgment. Post-fix programmatic-only catch rate: **62.5% (10/16)** with 0 false positives (up from 31.3%). Sonnet validator expected to catch most of the remaining 6 semantic slips in production. New fixes caught in audit: SSH port wrong, HTTPS port wrong, WEP outdated, access-list keyword overlap, subnet math 6 vs 8. 1 new UAT assertion (1993 total). Cache bumped to `netplus-v4.38.4`. |

Canonical id still used for history lookups/drilling/grouping; only the display text changed. **Explanation panel + Deep Dive panel restyled to forced white background + black text** (hardcoded `#ffffff` / `#111111`, bypassing theme vars) with a colored left-border accent (green/red/purple) to preserve correct/wrong/deep-dive signaling — user feedback that their brain reads white-on-black explanations better than the green/red tinted dark panels. `drillTopic()` now also opens the target chip's collapsed domain `<details>` accordion on the setup page, `scrollIntoView` centers it, and applies a temporary `.chip-flash` animation (1.3s pulse + scale) so you can see exactly where you landed — previously tapping a Topic Progress row would select a chip invisibly hidden inside a closed accordion. Extracted `renderResultsDifficultyBreakdown()` from `finish()` (84 → ~65 lines), `buildTopicDivePrompt()` from `showTopicDeepDive()` (83 → ~60 lines), and `buildWeightedTopicMap(historyEntries, now)` from `getReadinessScore()` (86 → ~73 lines). Long-function count: **11 → 8** (under tightened threshold of 8). Remaining offenders for a future refactor session: `fetchQuestions` (120), `submitExam` (117), `evaluateMilestones` (89), `renderCliSim` (92), `renderTopology` (131), `aiValidateQuestions` (86), `explainFurther` (101), and the elephant `renderAnalytics` (482). **Tech debt #17 fixed**: bulk-replaced inline `.style.*` assignments with CSS utility classes — `.is-hidden { display: none !important; }` and `.is-dimmed { opacity: 0.5 }`. All 74 `style.display = 'none'/'block'/'flex'/''` toggles became `classList.add/remove/toggle('is-hidden', ...)`, all 7 `style.opacity = '0.5'/'1'` toggles became `classList.toggle('is-dimmed', ...)`. Inline `.style.*` count: **117 → 37** (-80). Tech-debt monitor threshold tightened from 105 to 50 to lock in the win. **Important follow-up**: 17 elements in `index.html` had `style="display:none"` baked into the markup; a `classList.remove('is-hidden')` from JS could not override that inline style, so Playwright tests waiting on `subnet-next-btn`, `port-game`, `weak-banner`, `stats-card`, etc. all failed. All 17 inline `display:none` HTML attributes were converted to `class="... is-hidden"` so JS toggling actually shows the elements. Lesson: when you migrate JS toggling to a CSS class, audit the matching HTML markup for inline styles that would shadow the class. **Tech debt #23 fixed**: dead code sweep — removed unreferenced `ipToArr()` helper (replaced long ago by `octetsFromIp()`-style usage) and the unused `N10_009_OBJECTIVE_RE` constant (the actual objective validation in `validateQuestions` uses an inline substring regex with capture group for "Obj 1.4" / "1.4 — Routing" extraction, so the anchored constant was a duplicate that drifted out of use). UAT swapped the `N10_009_OBJECTIVE_RE` symbol assertion for a regex-pattern presence check. **Tech debt #20 fixed**: service worker now hard-caps the runtime cache at `CACHE_MAX_ENTRIES = 60` and FIFO-evicts via a new `trimCache()` helper called after every `cache.put`. 5xx responses are no longer cached and now fall back to the cached copy when available, so a Vercel/origin outage no longer breaks the offline app. Cache bumped to `netplus-v4.11.8`. **Tech debt #24 fixed**: new `.github/workflows/auto-add-to-board.yml` listens for `issues.opened/labeled/reopened` and adds the issue to Board #1 (`tech-debt`/`bug`) or Board #2 (`feature-idea`) via GraphQL `addProjectV2ItemById`. Replaces the unreliable built-in GitHub Projects auto-add workflow that did not fire for REST-API-created issues. Project IDs are looked up at runtime by project number so they're never hardcoded. Both this workflow and the existing tech-debt issue-creation block in `ci.yml` now use `secrets.PROJECT_TOKEN || secrets.GITHUB_TOKEN` — `PROJECT_TOKEN` is a PAT with the `project` scope (the default `GITHUB_TOKEN` lacks it, which is why the existing inline GraphQL block in the tech-debt job had been silently failing) |

| v4.31.1 | **Fix quiz question count bug** — Quiz sometimes generated 1 or 6 questions instead of the requested 5. Root cause: AI returns variable question counts, and the validation pipeline (`aiValidateQuestions` + `validateQuestions`) filters additional questions with no count enforcement. Fix: after validation, truncate to `qCount` if AI returned extras; if too many filtered out (<50% remaining), auto-retry with a fresh `fetchQuestions` call to backfill. Also enforces count cap on bulk quiz mode and cached fallback path. Cache bumped to `netplus-v4.31.1`. |

| v4.28.1 | **AI Generation Reliability Fix** — fixes "invalid topology" error when generating complex scenarios like "2 data centres connected via VPN". Root causes: (1) `max_tokens` was 4096 — complex topologies with VPN configs routinely exceeded this, causing truncated JSON that the parser couldn't handle. Bumped to 8192. (2) No retry mechanism — a single parse failure immediately showed an error. Now uses a two-attempt strategy: first attempt with full prompt, second attempt with a simplified focused prompt if the first fails. (3) Parser couldn't handle truncated JSON — added Stage 5 truncation repair that counts open/close braces/brackets and attempts to close them to salvage partial results. (4) Semantic expansion was too verbose — "data centres" expanded into a paragraph-long description that overwhelmed Haiku. Shortened all 16 expansions to concise device-type references. (5) "Output ONLY valid JSON" rule was buried at the end of the prompt (Rule 12) — moved to the very first line of the base prompt so the AI sees it before the lengthy device guide. (6) No debugging — added `console.log` for raw AI response text, stop_reason, and response length so truncation and parse failures are diagnosable in the browser console. New `_tbCallAiAndParse()` helper encapsulates the fetch+parse+logging cycle. 10 new UAT assertions (1091 total). Cache bumped to `netplus-v4.28.1`. |

| v4.23.1 | **Hotfix: double-click device to open config panel** — root cause: `tbOnDeviceMouseDown` called `e.preventDefault()` which suppresses the browser's native `dblclick` event, AND `tbRenderCanvas()` destroys/recreates all device DOM nodes after every mousedown, so the second click of a double-click lands on a freshly created element that never saw the first click. Fix: replaced the unreliable native `dblclick` listener (`tbAttachDoubleClick`) with a manual timestamp-based double-click detector inside `tbOnDeviceMouseDown` — tracks `tbLastClickDevId` + `tbLastClickTime`, fires `tbOpenConfigPanel(id)` if same device clicked within 400ms. Removed dead `tbAttachDoubleClick` function and its call site in `tbRenderCanvas`. Cache bumped to `netplus-v4.23.1`. |

| v4.21.0 | **Topology Builder Tier 3 — AI Coach (closes the TB 3-tier plan)** — ships the last tier on the original Topology Builder roadmap: an instructor-style AI walkthrough of whatever the user just built. Complements the Tier 2 static rules engine — grader for "is this design broken?", coach for "teach me *why* this design is good and how it maps to the exam." Tier 1+2+3 all now live in a single session today. (1) **Topology serializer** — new `tbSerializeTopology(state)` walks the device graph and emits a compact text description the LLM reads well: devices are grouped by type and assigned stable labels (e.g. `Firewall #1`, `Firewall #2` when duplicates exist), then two sections are emitted — `INVENTORY:` (one line per device type with counts) and `CONNECTIONS:` (one line per device listing neighbors with their cable type inline, e.g. `- Router → Firewall #1 (Fiber), Switch (Cat6)`). Orphan devices render as `(not connected)` so the coach can call them out. This shape avoids dumping raw JSON at the model, which tends to get LLMs to produce shallow observations. (2) **Response caching** — new `tbTopologyHash(state, scenarioId)` produces a deterministic short hash (djb2-style) over a simplified payload: scenario id + device types/positions (rounded to a 20px grid so micro-drags don't bust the cache) + sorted cable endpoints/types. Hash is used as a key in `STORAGE.TB_COACH_CACHE` (new `nplus_tb_coach_cache` localStorage entry). Responses are cached with a timestamp; `tbSaveCoachCache` trims to the 10 most recent entries. Cache hit → modal renders instantly with a `cached` pill next to the scenario title, no API call. This means re-opening a modal you just closed is free, and iterating a topology only bills for the meaningful changes. (3) **Coach entry point** — new async `tbCoachTopology()` (a) short-circuits on empty canvas with a toast, (b) short-circuits with a toast pointing to Settings if `STORAGE.KEY` is empty (no API call attempted), (c) checks cache and early-returns on hit, (d) shows the modal in loading state via `tbShowCoachModalLoading(scenario)` which renders a spinning ring + "Coach is analyzing your topology… (usually 3-5 seconds)" sub-line, (e) calls `CLAUDE_API_URL` with `CLAUDE_MODEL` (haiku 4.5), `max_tokens: 1500`, and a prompt that sets the instructor persona, feeds the scenario context + serialized topology, and asks for a strict JSON response with six keys: `tour` (2-3 sentence walkthrough), `strengths[]` (2-4 wins tied to objectives), `concerns[]` (2-4 things the static grader might miss), `upgrades[]` (2-3 actionable upgrades with rationale), `objectives[]` (2-4 N10-009 objectives exercised), `studyTip` (1 sentence pointing to what to drill next). Response is cleaned of any stray markdown fences (`\u0060\u0060\u0060json ... \u0060\u0060\u0060`), parsed with a JSON.parse + fallback `{...}` regex extract so the modal still works if the model wraps its output. Cached + rendered on success, `tbShowCoachModalError(msg)` on any failure path with a Retry button that just re-invokes `tbCoachTopology()`. (4) **Coach modal** — new `#tb-coach-modal` shares the overlay/card/backdrop styling from Tier 2's grade modal (class-reuse: `.tb-grade-modal`) but with a sky-blue accent palette distinct from the purple grader. Structure: coach head (cyan gradient band with scenario title + tour paragraph) → 4 severity-colored sections (Strengths green, Concerns amber, Upgrades sky, Objectives purple) each with bullet lists → final "Study next" callout in a dashed purple border box. New CSS block (~140 lines) covering `.tb-coach-loading`, `.tb-coach-spinner` (4px ring with top-color accent + `tb-coach-spin` keyframe), `.tb-coach-error`, `.tb-coach-head`, `.tb-coach-cached` (pill badge), `.tb-coach-section` + 4 section variants, `.tb-coach-list`, `.tb-coach-tip`, `.tb-tool-btn-coach` (sky-blue gradient toolbar button mirroring the purple `.tb-tool-btn-primary` from Tier 2). New 🤖 Coach button added to the toolbar between 🎓 Grade and 📷 Export PNG. Intro banner copy updated to drop the "Tier 3 adds an AI coach" promise since it's now live. 35 new UAT assertions covering the serializer output sections, all 7 new functions, cache trim behavior, API call shape, error handling, HTML wiring, and CSS presence. Total UAT: 780 → 815. Cache bumped to `netplus-v4.21.0`. |
| v4.20.0 | **Topology Builder Tier 2 — Auto-Grader + Scenario Mode + PNG Export** — closes the original Tier 2 scope (design validation) from the TB parent plan. Three features shipped together. (1) **Rules engine**: new `TB_GRADE_RULES` array of 12 rules (id/severity/label/hint/test), each `test(state)` inspecting `tbState.devices` + `tbState.cables` via three new graph helpers — `tbNeighborsOf(state, id)` returns the device objects on the other end of every cable touching `id`, `tbIsConnectedTo(state, id, type)` checks for a one-hop neighbor of a given type, `tbDevicesOfType(state, type)` filters the device list. Rules: `min-devices` (3+), `no-orphans`, `has-firewall` (critical), `cloud-behind-firewall` (critical — every cloud node must touch a firewall), `dmz-exists-if-public` (critical), `public-on-dmz` (critical — every public-* device must neighbor a dmz-switch and NOT a regular switch), `dmz-behind-firewall` (critical), `internal-behind-firewall` (warning — internal switch must touch a firewall or router), `wlc-wired-to-wap` (warning — does a 2-hop WLC→switch→WAP search so WLC/AP/switch triangle passes), `lb-fronts-servers` (warning — LB must neighbor 2+ servers or public-*), `ids-positioned` (info), `endpoints-on-internal` (warning — PC/printer/voip/iot must not touch dmz-switch). Severity-weighted deductions: critical -20, warning -10, info -5, floor at 0. Letter grade map: A (93+) / A- (87+) / B+ (80+) / B (73+) / C+ (65+) / C (58+) / D (50+) / F. `tbGradeTopology()` entry point runs the scenario-selected rule subset, appends synthetic critical rules for scenario device-count requirements, and calls `tbShowGradeModal()` which renders a fixed-overlay modal (`#tb-grade-modal`) with a score circle (color flips green/yellow/red at 87/70), pill counts (passed/critical/warnings/info), and 4 stacked sections (Critical / Warnings / Suggestions / Passed) each showing rule label + actionable hint. `tbCloseGradeModal()` closes the overlay; backdrop click also closes. (2) **Scenario mode**: new `TB_SCENARIOS` catalog with 5 scenarios — Free Build (all rules), Small Office (cloud→firewall→switch with 2+ PCs + printer), DMZ / Screened Subnet (full DMZ rule chain + public-* server requirement), Enterprise w/ IDS + LB (all rules + 2+ firewalls, IDS, LB, 2+ servers), Branch Office w/ Wireless (WLC + 2+ WAPs + 2+ PCs). Each scenario has `ruleIds` (which rules to run), `requires` (device-count hard requirements — `type: 'public-*'` wildcard matches any public-web/file/cloud), `requirements` (string list for display). New `tbSelectedScenario` state (defaults `'free'`). New `tbSetScenario(id)` updates state and calls `tbRenderScenarioPanel()` which populates `#tb-scenario-panel` with the scenario title, description, and requirements `<ul>` — hidden entirely in Free Build, shown above the canvas otherwise. Scenario device-count failures appear as critical rule rows labeled "Scenario requires N+ X (you have M)". New `<select id="tb-scenario-select">` in the toolbar wired to `tbSetScenario()`. `openTopologyBuilder()` now calls `tbRenderScenarioPanel()` on open so the panel restores with the current scenario. (3) **PNG export**: new `tbExportPNG()` clones the live `#tb-canvas` SVG, stamps explicit width/height attrs, prepends a dark `#0b1020` `<rect>` background (since the grid pattern is transparent), serializes with `XMLSerializer().serializeToString()`, base64-encodes via `btoa(unescape(encodeURIComponent(...)))` to survive multi-byte chars, feeds it through an `<img>` → `<canvas>` → `canvas.toBlob()` pipeline, and triggers a hidden `<a download>` click. Filename is `{topology_name_sanitized}_{timestamp}.png`. Zero external deps, pure browser APIs. New **🎓 Grade** primary button (`.tb-tool-btn-primary` gradient) and **📷 Export PNG** ghost button added to the toolbar. Intro banner copy updated to document the new Grade + Export capabilities. New CSS block (~170 lines) for `.tb-grade-modal` + `.tb-grade-backdrop` + `.tb-grade-card` + `.tb-grade-hero` + `.tb-grade-circle` + `.tb-grade-counts` + `.tb-grade-section` (severity-colored left borders for crit/warn/info/pass) + `.tb-scenario-panel` + `.tb-scenario-reqs` + `.tb-tool-btn-primary`. 44 new UAT assertions covering every rule id, every scenario id, all 3 new functions, HTML wiring, and CSS presence. Total UAT: 736 → 780. Cache bumped to `netplus-v4.20.0`. |
| v4.19.1 | **Topology Builder: DMZ Switch + clickable cable hitbox** — follow-up fixes after v4.19.0 shipped and the user built their first DMZ topology. The fat hitbox makes even thin fiber cables trivially clickable. The click handler now binds on `.tb-cable-hit` instead of `.tb-cable`, so once a cable is selected the user can press Del/Backspace to remove it (delete-selected logic was already in place, just unreachable due to the click target issue). | v4.19.0 | **Topology Builder: cable type picker, realistic cables, public-server devices for DMZ, compact icons** — five pieces of feedback after v4.18.3 shipped, bundled into one release. (2) **Realistic cable rendering** — cables were straight `<line>` elements, now they're `<path>` elements with a slight downward Q-curve drape (midpoint +16px) that makes them look like cables that sag under their own weight. Each cable renders as two stacked paths: a dark `#0b1020` sheath (width + 5px, 70% opacity, no pointer events) and an inner colored conductor at the type's `meta.width` and `meta.color`. Console cables render dashed (`stroke-dasharray: 6 4`) to distinguish rollover/mgmt from data. User can now wire a firewall → DMZ switch → public-web/file/cloud cluster → another firewall → internal switch to model a classic screened subnet. (4) **Compact canvas devices for 30-device layouts** — device rect shrunk 124×96 → 96×72, label font 16 → 13, icons wrapped in `<g transform="scale(0.72) translate(0,4)">` to fit the smaller box, label y-offset 34 → 26. `HALF_W`/`HALF_H` for cable edge-intersection dropped from 62/48 → 48/36. `tbOnMouseMove` bounds clamp dropped from 75/60 → 55/45 padding. | v4.18 | **Topology Builder Tier 1 — SVG canvas + device palette + cables + save/load (#74)** — first of 3 planned tiers for the visual network topology builder feature (parent #73, Tier 2 = config panels #75, Tier 3 = AI coach #76). New top-level `🔧 Topology Builder` menu button on the setup page launches a new `#page-topology-builder` with a 1200x700 SVG canvas (grid pattern background) and a left-side device palette containing 7 device types: Router, Switch, WAP, PC, Server, Firewall, Cloud. Each device type is defined in a single `TB_DEVICE_TYPES` map with `label`, `icon`, `color`, `short` — adding a new type is one entry. State is a single `tbState` object: `{ id, name, devices: [{id, type, x, y}], cables: [{id, from, to}], created, updated }`, single source of truth, all rendering derives from it. Interactions: **drag from palette** (HTML5 drag API) drops device at cursor position (coordinates translated from client space to SVG viewBox via `createSVGPoint` + `getScreenCTM`); **click device A → click device B** draws a cable (second click completes, clicking the same device cancels); **drag a placed device** moves it within canvas bounds (50/40 padding enforced); **click empty canvas** deselects; **Delete/Backspace** removes selected device (cascade removes any cables touching it) or selected cable; **Escape** cancels current selection and pending cable. Guardrails: **15-device cap** (toast when full), **self-loop prevention**, **duplicate cable detection** (either direction), **device cap enforced before add**, **input field detection** so Delete inside an input doesn't nuke the topology. Persistence: **`STORAGE.TOPOLOGY_DRAFT`** auto-saves on every change (drop, move, cable, delete) so accidental reload never loses work; **`STORAGE.TOPOLOGIES`** holds up to 5 named saves with FIFO eviction by `updated` timestamp when the 6th is added; **Save As** prompts for a name and upserts by topology id; **Load** dropdown rebuilds from saves with device-count badges; **New** prompts to confirm if the canvas has devices. Mobile nudge: viewport < 900px width shows a friendly "Topology Builder works best on desktop" callout with an "Open Anyway" override that sets `tbMobileOverride = true` and continues. Builder state is prefixed `tb*` (tbState, tbSelectedId, tbPendingCableFrom, tbDragging, tbPaletteDrag, tbMobileOverride, tbCanvasHandlersAttached, tbKeyHandlerAttached) to avoid collision with the existing PBQ `topoDevices`/`selectedTopoDevice` state used by the drag-into-zones question type. | v4.15 | **Port Drill: Secure Pairs mode (#30)** — fourth Port Drill mode joining Timed/Endless/Family. Dedicated drill for the Network+ secure↔insecure protocol pairings (HTTP↔HTTPS, FTP↔FTPS/SFTP, Telnet↔SSH, SMTP↔SMTPS/587, LDAP↔LDAPS, POP3↔POP3S, IMAP↔IMAPS). New `securePairs` static dataset with 9 mappings — FTP and SMTP appear twice (each has two valid secure equivalents) with `qualifier` strings ("over SSL/TLS", "over SSH", "with implicit TLS", "using STARTTLS submission") to disambiguate the prompt and `siblingProto` to exclude the alternate from distractors. New `nextPortPairsQ()` randomizes between two question formats: **port-pick** ("HTTPS is the secure version of HTTP. Which port does HTTPS use?") and **proto-pick** ("Which protocol replaces FTP (port 21) over SSH?"). Distractors come from the secure/insecure pool, deduped by the answered field, with the sibling protocol excluded so users never have to choose between two technically-correct answers. Timeless like family mode — one wrong answer ends the streak. New `STORAGE.PORT_PAIRS_BEST` (`nplus_port_pairs_best`) tracks pairs-mode best independently from Timed/Endless/Family. `setPortMode()`, `beginPortDrill()`, `pickPort()`, and `endPortDrill()` all extended for the new mode; `pickPort()` ends the run on wrong for both endless and pairs. New "&#128274; Secure Pairs" button on the pregame mode toggle. Cache bumped to `netplus-v4.15.0` |

Single `fetchQuestions` calls become unreliable above ~20 Qs, so the new `startBulkQuiz(count)` mirrors `startExam`'s batching: chunks the request into 18-Q batches with 2 retries each, drives the existing `#load-progress` bar, then runs the same `aiValidateQuestions` → `validateQuestions` → `injectPBQs` pipeline as `startQuiz` before flipping to the quiz page. `applyPreset()` routes `bulk30/bulk60/bulk100` to `startBulkQuiz` and clears all `#count-group` chip highlights (no chip matches 30/60/100). Topic forced to Mixed, difficulty forced to Exam Level. Cache bumped to `netplus-v4.14.0` |
| v4.12.1 | **Family Drill split into its own Port Drill mode** — user feedback on v4.12.0 was that the 20% family-Q sprinkle into the existing Timed/Endless flow felt jarring and broke the rhythm of single-port memorization. `nextPortQ()` reverted to the original 50/50 port/proto split with no family branch. New `'family'` value in `portMode` joins `'timed'` and `'endless'`; new "Family Drill" button on the pregame mode toggle (`#port-mode-family`). `setPortMode()` handles all 3 modes — family hides the timer block, shows "BEST STREAK" label, swaps in a family-specific description ("No timer. Each question asks you to select every port in a protocol family — one wrong submission ends the streak."). `beginPortDrill()` routes to `nextPortFamilyQ()` when `portMode === 'family'` and never starts the countdown timer. `submitPortFamilyAnswer()` treats family as endless-style: one wrong submission ends the streak, never deducts time, and re-rolls another family Q on success (no fall-through to single-Q rotation). New `STORAGE.PORT_FAMILY_BEST` (`nplus_port_family_best`) tracks the family-mode best independently from `PORT_BEST` (timed) and `PORT_STREAK_BEST` (endless). `endPortDrill()` labels the final score "family streak" in family mode. Cache bumped to `netplus-v4.12.1` |
